Shahadat — Testimony

Istihsan for Sons' Testimony on Father's Will
Hanafi istihsan ruling on testimony about a will's executor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi istihsan rule for sons' testimony on a father's will, distinguish it from the qiyas in agency, and apply the distinction to determine when such testimony is accepted or rejected.

Core Idea
Testimony that indirectly benefits the witness is accepted in executorship (wasi) though rejected in agency (wakala).

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents a nuanced ruling: normally, testimony that draws personal benefit (jar al-manfa'a) is rejected. However, when two sons testify that their father appointed a specific executor (wasi), and that executor confirms, their testimony is accepted by istihsan (juristic preference). The key is that the benefit is indirect and serves the deceased's intent, unlike the direct benefit in agency cases. This lesson unpacks the qiyas and the istihsan reasoning, helping you understand when Hanafi law prioritizes public interest over strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule on testimony and benefit
Recall that Hanafi law rejects testimony that draws any benefit to the witness (jar al-manfa'a). This is based on preserving witness integrity.
This rule is qiyasi (analogical) and applies broadly.
2
Examine the qiyas to agency (wakala)
The text compares the case of sons testifying about an executor (wasi) to sons testifying about an agent (wakil). In agency, the testimony is rejected because the witness benefits directly (e.g., collecting a debt).
The illa (effective cause) is the witness's direct benefit.
3
Understand the istihsan exception for executorship
For the wasi, the benefit to the sons is indirect (proper management of the estate). The executor is a trustee of the deceased, not an agent of the heirs. Istihsan overrides qiyas to facilitate the execution of wills.
The exception applies only when the alleged executor also claims the role; if he denies, the testimony is rejected.
4
Apply the distinction to new scenarios
Consider: if the sons testify that the father appointed a guardian for their property, or a trustee for a charity. Analyze whether the benefit is direct or indirect based on the nature of the appointment.
The key is whether the appointee serves the deceased's purpose or the heirs' personal interests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شهد ابنان أن الأب أوصى إلى زيد، وهو يدعيه صحت (ولو شهد ابنان أن الأب أوصى إلى زيد، وهو يدعيه صحت) (1) صورته : إنّ رجلاً مات وترك ابنين فادعيا أنّ أباهما أوصى إلى رجل، والرجل يدعي الوصيّة جازت شهادتهما؛ ولئن أنكر هذا الرجل تلك الوصيَّة لا تقبل شهادتهما، كما لا تقبل شهادتهما إنّ أباهما الغائب قد وكَّل هذا الرجل بقبض دينه، وادعى الوكيل ذلك. وكذا إذا شهد الموصي إليهما أو لهما أولاً لغريمان لهما عليه دين، أو عليهما له دين أنه أوصى إلى هذا الرجل تجوز هذه الشهادة استحساناً، والقياس أن لا تجوز؛ لأنها تجر منفعة إلى الشاهد بإقامة من يحفظ ماله أو من يستوفي منه أو من تبرؤ ذمته بالتسليم إليه، أو من يعينه بالقيام على الوصية. والشهادة التي تجرُّ منفعة لا تقبل، فصار نظير مسألة الوكالة، ووجه الاستحسان ما ذكره الشارح؛ لقوله: بخلاف الإيصاء؛ لأنَّ الوصي...
And if two sons testify that the father appointed Zayd as executor, and he (Zayd) also claims it, it is valid. Its scenario: A man died leaving two sons, and they claimed that their father appointed a man as executor, and the man claims the executorship; their testimony is permissible. But if this man denies that executorship, their testimony is not accepted. Similarly, their testimony is not accepted if they claim that their absent father had appointed this man as agent to collect his debt, and the agent claims that. Likewise, if the person appointed as executor first testifies for them (the sons) or they for him, in case of creditors having a debt on them or they having a debt on the creditor, that he appointed this man as executor, this testimony is valid by istihsan, while by qiyas it would not be valid, because it draws benefit to the witness by establishing someone who preserves his wealth, or collects from him, or frees his liability by payment to him, or assists him in managing the will. And testimony that draws benefit is not accepted, so it becomes analogous to the case of agency. The basis of istihsan is what the commentator mentioned, because he said: contrary to a will, because the executor...
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage discusses an exception in Hanafi law regarding the testimony of two sons about their father's will. Normally, testimony that benefits the witness is rejected (e.g., agency cases). However, if two sons testify that their father appointed a specific person as executor (wasi), and that person also claims the role, their testimony is accepted by istihsan (juristic preference). The reasoning: unlike an agent (wakil), an executor has authority to handle the estate and the sons have a direct interest in proper management. The benefit to the witnesses is indirect and not purely personal, unlike agency where the witness might directly benefit from the agent's actions. The text explains that if the alleged executor denies the appointment, the sons' testimony is not accepted, because then they would be testifying for themselves (to enforce the will against the denier). Also, if the sons claim their absent father appointed an agent to collect a debt, and the agent affirms, the testimony is rejected. The general qiyas (analogy) would reject all such testimony due to conflict of interest, but istihsan allows it in the specific case of executorship because of the public interest in facilitating the execution of wills and the unique role of the executor.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to a stronger reason (like need or custom). Here, it allows testimony despite apparent benefit to the witness.
الوصي (al-wasi): Executor of a will; person appointed to manage the deceased's estate according to the will.
جر المنفعة (jar al-manfa'a): Drawing benefit (to the witness); a ground for rejecting testimony if the benefit is direct and personal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the testimony of two sons that their father appointed an executor accepted in Hanafi fiqh, despite benefiting them?
A) Because the sons are always considered trustworthy.
B) Because the appointment of an executor is obligatory.
C) Because the benefit is indirect and the executor is a neutral trustee.
D) Because the father's will overrides all conflicts.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law accepts sons' testimony about a father's will executor by istihsan because the benefit is indirect and furthers the deceased's intent, overriding the qiyas that rejects benefitting testimony.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony of Sons on Father's Will Appointing Executor
Ruling on two sons' testimony about father's will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of heirs regarding appointment of an executor, explain the reasoning of qiyas and istihsan, and identify when the testimony is accepted or rejected.

Core Idea
Testimony that benefits the witness is usually rejected, but istihsan accepts it when the judge could have appointed the executor himself.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh corpus addresses a nuanced issue in the law of testimony (shahada): when two sons testify that their deceased father appointed a man as executor (wasi), is their testimony accepted? The answer depends on whether the appointed executor claims the role. The author (al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah) presents both the strict analogical reasoning (qiyas) and the preferred juristic reasoning (istihsan). Understanding this distinction is key to grasping how Hanafi jurists balance textual principles with practical considerations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and default ruling
Read the opening of the Arabic passage: two sons testify that their father appointed an executor. The default ruling by strict analogy (qiyas) would be rejection because the testimony brings benefit to the sons. But the text immediately says 'jāzat shahādatuhumā' (their testimony is valid) by istihsan.
Note the contrast: qiyas would reject, istihsan accepts. This is the central tension.
2
Analyze the qiyas (analogy) with agency
The author draws an analogy with the case of agency (wakāla): if two sons testify that their absent father appointed an agent to collect a debt, that testimony is rejected. The common factor (ʿilla) is that the witness benefits by having the executor/agent manage the estate or collect debts. So by qiyas, both should be rejected.
The ʿilla is the benefit to the witness. See the qiyas panel in the toolbox.
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning based on judge's authority
The author explains why executorship is different: the judge can appoint an executor himself, but cannot appoint an agent for an absent person. Accepting the testimony in the executor case is like the judge appointing him; the benefit to the sons is incidental. In agency, the judge cannot create that relationship, so the benefit becomes decisive and testimony is rejected.
Key phrase: 'li-anna al-qāḍī yamliku naṣb al-waṣī' (the judge has authority to appoint the executor).
4
Apply to the five categories of witnesses
The text lists five categories of witnesses (creditors, debtors, legatees, executors, and heirs) whose testimony about the appointment is accepted by istihsan when the executor claims it. But if the executor denies, it is rejected because the judge cannot compel anyone to accept executorship.
Memorize the five categories: they all share a potential conflict of interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولو شهد ابنان ...الخ ؛ صورته : إنّ رجلاً مات وترك ابنين فادعيا أنّ أباهما أوصى إلى رجل، والرجل يدعي الوصيّة جازت شهادتهما ؛ ولئن أنكر هذا الرجل تلك الوصيَّة لا تقبل شهادتهما ، كما لا تقبل شهادتهما إنّ أباهما الغائب قد وكَّل هذا الرجل بقبض دينه ، وادعى الوكيل ذلك. وكذا إذا شهد الموصي إليهما أو لهما أولاً لغريمان لهما عليه دين، أو عليهما له دين أنه أوصى إلى هذا الرجل تجوز هذه الشهادة استحساناً، والقياس أن لا تجوز؛ لأنها تجر منفعة إلى الشاهد بإقامة من يحفظ ماله أو من يستوفي منه أو من تبرؤ ذمته بالتسليم إليه، أو من يعينه بالقيام على الوصية. والشهادة التي تجرُّ منفعة لا تقبل، فصار نظير مسألة الوكالة، ووجه الاستحسان ما ذكره الشارح ; لقوله : بخلاف الإيصاء ; لأنَّ الوصي... وإن أنكر لا كشهادة دائني الميت، ومديونيه، والموصى لهما، ووصيه على الإيصاء، وإن شهدا أنّ أباهما الغائب وكلَهُ بقبض دينه، وادعى الوكيل، أو جَحَدَ ردت. (وإن أنكر لا ) : أي شهدا أن الأب جعل زيداً وصيَّاً في الشركة، وهو يدعي وَصَي صحت شهادتهما ، وإنما قال : وهو يدعيه ; لأنه لو أنكر لا تقبل الشهادة، كشهادة دائني الميت، ومديونيه، والموصى لهما، ووصيه على الإيصاء) : أي صح شهادة هؤلاء إذا ادعى زيد أنه وصي. (وإن شهدا أن أباهما الغائب وكلهُ بقبض دينه ، وادعى الوكيل، أو جَحَدَ ردَّت) ; لأنَّ القاضي لا يَمْلِكُ نصب الوكيل عن الغائب ، فلو ثبت الوكالة، يثبت بشهادتهما ، فلا يمكن ثبوتُها بها لمكان التهمة بخلاف الإيصاء ; لأنَّ الوصيَّ إذا ادعى يكون قبول الشهادة كتعيين الوصي، والقاضي يملك ذلك. قوله : وإن أنكر لا ; أي وإن أنكر زيد إيصاءه لا تصح شهادتهما ; لأنَّ القاضي لا يملك إجبار أحدٍ على قبول الوصية. قوله : كشهادة دائني الميت...الخ ; هاهنا خمس مسائل : الغريمان لهما على الميت دين، والغريمان عليهما للميت دين، والموصي لهما، والموصى إليهما، والوارثان ، وشهد كل فريق أنَّ الميت أوصى إلى هذا ، وهو يطلب ذلك جازت الشهادة استحساناً. وفي القياس : لا يجوز ، وإن أنكر الوصي ذلك لم تجز قياساً واستحساناً. قوله : لأن القاضي....الخ ; تقريره : إنَّ القاضي لا يملك نصب الوكيل عن الغائب، فلو ثبت لثبت بشهادتهما، وهي غير موجبة لأجل التهمة فبطلت، بخلاف مسألة الإيصاء، فإنَّ للقاضي ولاية نصب الوصيّ إذا كان الوصي طالباً، وكان الموت معروفاً. فيكفي القاضي بهذه الشهادة مؤنة التعيين ، وزكياه بشهادتهما، إذ لولا شهادتهما كان يتأمل فيمن يعين، وفيمن يصلح ، فيعينُ مَن تثبتُ صلاحيته نظراً للميت، وإن لم يوص ; لأنه نصب ناظراً فلم يثبت بهذه الشهادة شيء لم يكن له فعله، ونظيرها القرعة، فإنّها ليست بموجبةٍ شيئاً لم يكن له لولا القُرعة، ومع هذا جاز استعمالها ; تطيباً للقلوب ونفياً للتهمة عن القاضي.
His saying: 'If two sons testify that the father appointed an executor to Zayd and he claims it, it is valid.' Its form: A man died leaving two sons who claim that their father appointed a man as executor, and the man claims the executorship; their testimony is valid. But if this man denies that executorship, their testimony is not accepted, just as their testimony is not accepted if their absent father had appointed this man to collect his debt and the agent claims it. Likewise, if the two sons – who are either creditors of the deceased or debtors to him, or legatees or executors, or heirs – testify that he appointed this man as executor, this testimony is valid by istihsan, while by qiyas it is not valid because it brings benefit to the witness: by appointing someone to preserve his wealth, or to collect from him, or to free his liability by delivery to him, or to assist him in managing the will. Testimony that brings benefit is not accepted, so it becomes analogous to the case of agency. The reasoning for istihsan is what the commentator mentioned: 'Unlike the appointment of an executor, because the executor...' And if he denies, it is not accepted, like the testimony of the deceased's creditors, debtors, legatees, and his executor regarding the appointment. If they testify that their absent father appointed him to collect his debt and the agent claims it or denies it, it is rejected. (And if he denies, it is not): i.e., if they testify that the father made Zayd an executor in the partnership, and he claims executorship, their testimony is valid. He only said 'and he claims it' because if he denies, the testimony is not accepted, like the testimony of the deceased's creditors, debtors, legatees, and his executor regarding the appointment: i.e., the testimony of these people is valid when Zayd claims he is the executor. (And if they testify that their absent father appointed him to collect his debt, and the agent claims it or denies it, it is rejected) because the judge does not have the authority to appoint an agent for an absent person. So if the agency is established, it would be established by their testimony, but it cannot be established due to the suspicion of self-interest, unlike the appointment of an executor because when the executor claims, accepting the testimony is like appointing the executor, and the judge has that authority. His saying: 'And if he denies, it is not': i.e., if Zayd denies the appointment, their testimony is not valid because the judge cannot compel anyone to accept executorship. His saying: 'Like the testimony of the deceased's creditors...' Here are five cases: the two creditors who have a debt from the deceased, the two debtors who owe a debt to the deceased, the two legatees, the two executors, and the two heirs. Each party testified that the deceased appointed this man as executor while he is seeking it; their testimony is valid by istihsan. By qiyas, it is not valid. If the executor denies that, it is not valid by qiyas and istihsan. His saying: 'Because the judge...' its explanation: The judge does not have authority to appoint an agent for an absent person, so if it were established, it would be established by their testimony, but that is not valid due to suspicion of self-interest. Unlike the case of appointment of an executor, because the judge has authority to appoint an executor if the executor is a claimant and the death is known. So through this testimony, the judge is spared the burden of selection, and they have proven his suitability by their testimony. Without their testimony, he would deliberate on whom to appoint and who is suitable, and then appoint someone whose suitability is established with regard to the deceased, even if he did not appoint; because he is appointing a supervisor, so nothing is proven by this testimony that he could not do. Analogous to this is casting lots, which does not prove anything that would not be possible without the lot, yet it is used to please hearts and remove suspicion from the judge.
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter of testimony (shahada) in Hanafi fiqh, specifically addressing when the testimony of two sons regarding their deceased father's appointment of an executor (wasi) is accepted. The author explains the scenario: if the executor himself claims the appointment, the sons' testimony is accepted; if he denies it, the testimony is rejected. This is contrasted with the case of agency (wakala), where even if the agent claims the appointment, the testimony is rejected. The difference lies in the authority of the judge: the judge can appoint an executor himself (since he has the general power to appoint a supervisor for the deceased's estate), so the sons' testimony serves as a recommendation that spares the judge from having to search for a suitable person. In contrast, the judge cannot appoint an agent for an absent principal, so accepting the testimony would effectively create a legal relationship that the judge cannot otherwise create, leading to suspicion of self-interest (tuhma). The passage also lists five categories of witnesses (creditors, debtors, legatees, executors, and heirs) whose testimony about the appointment is accepted by istihsan (juristic preference) but would be rejected by strict qiyas due to the benefit they derive from the appointment. The reasoning for istihsan is that the judge's authority to appoint the executor makes the testimony a mere recommendation, not a conclusive establishment of rights. The commentary concludes with an analogy to casting lots (qur'a), which is permissible even though it is not a source of rights, because it removes suspicion and pleases hearts.

Key Terms
الوَصِيَّة (al-wasiyya): A bequest or appointment of an executor to manage the deceased's estate.
الوَصِي (al-wasi): An executor appointed by the deceased to handle the estate, such as managing property, paying debts, and executing bequests.
الاسْتِحْسَان (al-istihsan): A method of juristic preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) due to a stronger consideration, often based on custom, necessity, or a higher legal principle.
القِيَاس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause ('illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two sons testify that their deceased father appointed Zayd as executor, but Zayd denies it. According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, is their testimony accepted?
A) Yes, because the sons are credible heirs.
B) Yes, because the judge can still appoint Zayd based on the testimony.
C) No, because the judge cannot compel Zayd to accept executorship.
D) No, because the testimony brings benefit to the sons.

Key Takeaway
The testimony of heirs about the appointment of an executor is accepted by istihsan if the executor claims it, because the judge can appoint him anyway, making the benefit to the witnesses incidental.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Testimony on Executor vs Agent: The Role of Judicial Authority
Ruling on testimony for executorship vs agency with istihsan reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony regarding executor (wasi) and agent (wakil) appointments and explain why the difference hinges on the judge’s authority.

Core Idea
Testimony on executorship is accepted because the judge can act; on agency rejected because judge lacks authority.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh commentary addresses a subtle distinction: two witnesses testify that an absent father appointed a certain person as his executor (wasi), and that person claims the executorship. According to the Hanafi school, that testimony is accepted. However, if the same witnesses testify that the father appointed an agent (wakil) to collect a debt from him, and the agent either claims or denies, the testimony is rejected. Why the difference? The key lies in the judge’s authority. Let’s walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
First, note the two distinct cases: (1) witnesses testify that the deceased appointed Zaid as executor, and Zaid claims it; (2) witnesses testify that an absent father appointed someone as agent for debt collection. In case 1 testimony is accepted; in case 2 it is rejected.
The commentary also includes cases where the executor denies — then testimony is rejected. Focus on the accepted vs rejected baseline.
2
Understand the Qiyas (Analogical) Ruling
By analogy (qiyas), testimony from interested parties (creditors, debtors, etc.) should be rejected due to suspicion (tuhma). But the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to accept it in the executor case, creating a departure from analogy.
The text mentions five categories of interested parties whose testimony would be accepted by istihsan in executorship matters.
3
Trace the 'Illa (Effective Cause) for the Difference
The judge has authority to appoint an executor for a deceased person; therefore, accepting testimony to establish executorship is like allowing the judge to make that appointment based on recommendation. For an agent, the judge cannot appoint an agent for an absent living person; thus testimony would create a right (agency) solely on the basis of suspicious evidence, which is prohibited.
The analogy with lottery (qur'a): it does not create new rights but eliminates suspicion.
4
Apply the Distinction to New Cases
Extend the principle: whenever the judge has the authority to directly appoint someone (like executor), testimony from interested parties may be accepted if it helps the judge decide. When the judge lacks such authority, the testimony is rejected because it would create a right from suspicious evidence.
This is a Hanafi-specific ruling based on the scope of judicial authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أنكر لا كشهادة دائني الميت، ومديونيه، والموصى لهما، ووصيه على الإيصاء، وإن شهدا أن أباهما الغائب وكلَهُ بقبض دينه، وادعى الوكيل، أو جَحَدَ ردت ; لأنَّ القاضي لا يَمْلِكُ نصب الوكيل عن الغائب ، فلو ثبت الوكالة، يثبت بشهادتهما ، فلا يمكن ثبوتُها بها لمكان التهمة بخلاف الإيصاء ؛ لأنَّ الوصيَّ إذا ادعى يكون قبول الشهادة كتعيين الوصي، والقاضي يملك ذلك. ١ ] قوله : وإن أنكر لا ؛ أي وإن أنكر زيد إيصاءه لا تصح شهادتهما ؛ لأنَّ القاضي لا يملك إجبار أحدٍ على قبول الوصية. [٢]قوله : كشهادة دائني الميت...الخ ؛ هاهنا خمس مسائل : الغريمان لهما على الميت دين، والغريمان عليهما للميت دين، والموصي لهما، والموصى إليهما، والوارثان ، وشهد كل فريق أنَّ الميت أوصى إلى هذا ، وهو يطلب ذلك جازت الشهادة استحساناً. وفي القياس : لا يجوز ، وإن أنكر الوصي ذلك لم تجز قياساً واستحساناً. (٣) قوله : لأن القاضي....الخ ؛ تقريره : إنَّ القاضي لا يملك نصب الوكيل عن الغائب، فلو ثبت لثبت بشهادتهما، وهي غير موجبة لأجل التهمة فبطلت، بخلاف مسألة الإيصاء، فإنَّ للقاضي ولاية نصب الوصيّ إذا كان الوصي طالباً، وكان الموت معروفاً. فيكفي القاضي بهذه الشهادة مؤنة التعيين ، وزكياه بشهادتهما، إذ لولا شهادتهما كان يتأمل فيمن يعين، وفيمن يصلح ، فيعينُ مَن تثبتُ صلاحيته نظراً للميت، وإن لم يوص ؛ لأنه نصب ناظراً فلم يثبت بهذه الشهادة شيء لم يكن له فعله، ونظيرها القرعة، فإنّها ليست بموجبةٍ شيئاً لم يكن له لولا القُرعة، ومع هذا جاز استعمالها ؛ تطيباً للقلوب ونفياً للتهمة عن القاضي.
And if he denies, it is not accepted, like the testimony of the creditors of the deceased, and his debtors, and the two legatees, and his executor regarding the will. And if they testify that their absent father appointed an agent to collect his debt, and the agent claims or denies, it is rejected; because the judge does not have the authority to appoint an agent for an absent person. If the agency were established, it would be established by their testimony, but it cannot be established due to suspicion, unlike the case of executorship because when the executor claims, accepting the testimony is like appointing the executor, and the judge has the authority to do that. [1] His statement: 'And if he denies' means if Zaid denies his executorship, their testimony is not valid because the judge does not have the power to compel anyone to accept executorship. [2] His statement: 'like the testimony of the creditors of the deceased...' etc. Here are five cases: two creditors who have a debt against the deceased, two debtors who owe a debt to the deceased, two legatees, two executors, and two heirs. Each team testified that the deceased made a will to this person, and he claims it; the testimony is valid by istihsan. By qiyas it is not valid. And if the executor denies it, it is not valid by qiyas and istihsan. (3) His statement: 'because the judge...' etc. Its explanation: The judge does not have the authority to appoint an agent for an absent person. Therefore, if it were established, it would be established by their testimony, and it is not effective due to suspicion, so it becomes invalid. Unlike the case of executorship, because the judge has the authority to appoint an executor if the executor is claimant and the death is known. So this testimony suffices the judge for the trouble of appointment, and they [the witnesses] recommend him by their testimony, because without their testimony he would consider whom to appoint and who is suitable, so he appoints one whose suitability is proven in the interest of the deceased, even if he did not make a will; because he appoints a supervisor. So nothing is established by this testimony that he could not have done without it. Its analogy is the lottery, for it does not establish anything that would not be established without the lot, yet it is permissible to use it to satisfy hearts and remove suspicion from the judge.
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage discusses rulings on testimony regarding the appointment of an executor (wasi) and an agent (wakil). The type is a ruling with proof, where the commentary expands on the matn. The passage begins by stating that if witnesses testify that a father appointed Zaid as executor, and Zaid claims the executorship, their testimony is accepted. However, if Zaid denies it, the testimony is rejected, similar to the testimony of creditors, debtors, legatees, and executors regarding a will. The reason is that the judge cannot compel someone to accept executorship. Next, if witnesses testify that an absent father appointed an agent to collect a debt, and the agent either claims or denies the agency, the testimony is rejected. This is because the judge does not have the authority to appoint an agent for an absent person. If the agency were to be established, it would be solely through their testimony, but due to suspicion of self-interest (tuhma), that testimony is not accepted. In contrast, in the case of executorship, if the executor claims it, accepting the testimony is akin to the judge appointing the executor, which the judge has the authority to do. The commentary then lists five categories of interested parties (creditors, debtors, etc.) and explains that their testimony is accepted by istihsan (juristic preference) even though qiyas would reject it. Finally, the passage provides an analogy with the lottery (qur'a): the lottery does not create a new right but is used to eliminate suspicion and satisfy hearts, similar to how this testimony is accepted to ease the judge's appointment process.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-waṣī): An executor appointed by the deceased to manage his affairs after death; the person tasked with carrying out the will.
الوكيل (al-wakīl): An agent appointed to act on behalf of another, here specifically for collecting a debt from an absent person.
التهمة (al-tuhma): Suspicion of self-interest or bias on the part of the witness that may affect the credibility of testimony.
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning where a ruling is preferred over qiyas due to a stronger evidence or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when do interested parties' witnesses regarding executorship fail to establish the executor's appointment?
A) When the executor denies the claim
B) When the witnesses are creditors of the deceased
C) When the executor is absent
D) When the judge is biased

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony from interested parties regarding executorship because the judge can act on it; but rejects testimony for agency because the judge cannot appoint an agent for an absent person.

The Ruling on Pure Impugnment (Jarh Mujarrad) in Testimony
Defines jarh mujarrad and explains why such testimony is not accepted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of pure impugnment (jarh mujarrad) and explain why the Hanafi school does not accept testimony based on it.

Core Idea
A testimony that only shows a witness's sinfulness, without establishing a legal right, is inadmissible.

This passage clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi law of testimony: not every charge of fisq (sinfulness) against a witness is enough to disqualify them. The text defines pure impugnment (jarh mujarrad) and explains the rationale: the judge can only adjudicate matters that lead to an enforceable ruling. Pure impugnment, being unenforceable, is rejected. Understanding this concept prevents conflation of mere allegation with legally sufficient evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the term 'jarh mujarrad' and its definition in the passage. Note the linguistic and technical meanings.
The passage gives both linguistic ('speaking ill') and technical ('revealing fisq') definitions.
2
Distinguish pure from non-pure impugnment
Pure impugnment does not establish a legal right for Allah or a person; non-pure does. Identify the key condition: the impugnment must entail an enforceable consequence.
Non-pure impugnment can lead to hadd or financial liability.
3
Analyze the examples provided
Review the list of what constitutes pure impugnment (e.g., 'he is fasiq', 'eats riba') and what constitutes non-pure (e.g., testimony leading to hadd or financial obligation).
The examples help internalize the boundary.
4
Understand the talil (rationale)
The passage states that pure impugnment is not accepted because it is not subject to judicial ruling (la yadkhul tahta al-hukm). The judge cannot enforce mere sinfulness.
This is a foundational principle of Hanafi fiqh: the judge's authority is limited to enforceable matters.
5
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Given a new accusation, first check whether it establishes a legal right. If not, it is pure impugnment and inadmissible.
This step reinforces the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كالشهادة على جرح مجرد، وهو ما يُفسقُ الشاهد ولم يوجب حقاً للشرع أو العبد ، مثل : هو فاسق ، أو آكل الربا، أو أنه استأجرهم): صورة المسألة : أن المدعي إذا أقام البينة على العدالة، فأقام الخصم البينة على الجرح إن كان الجرح جرحاً مجرَّداً لا يعتبرُ بينة الجرح بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن الموت معروفاً؛ لأنه حينئذ لا يملك القاضي نصب الوصي إلا بهذه البينة فتصير الشهادة موجبة ، فتبطل لمعنى التهمة، وهو جرُّ المنفعة إلى الشاهد (1) ١ ] قوله : كالشهادة ؛ أي كما لا تقبل الشهادة على جرح مجرد الجرح : بفتح الجيم لغة، من جرحه بلسانه جرحاً : عابه، وانتقصه، ومنه جَرَحْتُ الشاهد : إذا أظهرت فيه ما تردُّ به شهادته. كذا في «المصباح المنير». وفي اصطلاح الفقهاء : إظهارُ فسق الشاهد، وإن لم يتضمن ذلك إيجاب حق الله تعالى، أو للعبد، فهو جرح مجرد ، وإن تضمن إثبات حق الله تعالى أو للعبد فهو غيرُ مجرد. كذا في «البحر» (۳) ، وهو المراد من قوله : وهو ؛ أي الجرح المجرَّد بالفسق. الشاهد ؛ أي يظهر فسق الشاهد. ولم يوجب حقاً للشرع ؛ كوجوب الحد. أو العبد ؛ كوجوب المال ، فلو أوجبه تقبل مثل أن يشهدوا. هو ؛ أي الشاهد فاسق. أو آكل الربا، أو أنه استأجرهم، أو شارب خمر في وقت أو زان في وقت، أو على إقرارهم أنهم شهدوا بزور، أو إن المدعي مبطل في هذه الدعوى، أو إنه لا شهادةً لهم على المدعى عليه في هذه الحادثة. وإنما لا تقبل هذه الشهادة ؛ لأنَّ الفسق المجرَّد مما لا يدخل تحت الحكم، وليس في وسع القاضي إلزامه، والبينة إنما تقبلُ على ما يدخل تحت الحكم، وفي وسع القاضي إلزامه.
Like testimony on pure impugnment (jarh mujarrad), which is what renders the witness impious but does not establish a right for the Shari'ah or for a person, such as: 'he is impious,' or 'he consumes riba,' or 'that he hired them.' The scenario: If the plaintiff establishes evidence of integrity, and the opponent brings evidence of impugnment; if the impugnment is pure impugnment, the evidence of impugning is not considered, unlike when the death is not known; because then the judge does not have the authority to appoint an executor except through this evidence, so the testimony becomes effective, and it becomes invalid due to suspicion, which is drawing benefit to the witness. (1) [1] His statement: 'like testimony'; i.e., just as testimony on pure impugnment is not accepted. Jarh: linguistically, with a fatha on the jim, from jarahahu bi-lisanihi jarhan: to insult and depreciate him. From this, jarah-tu al-shahid: if you reveal something in him that rejects his testimony. This is stated in al-Misbah al-Munir. In the terminology of the jurists: it is revealing the fisq of the witness. If it does not entail establishing a right of Allah or of a person, it is pure impugnment. If it entails establishing a right of Allah or of a person, it is not pure. This is stated in al-Bahr. And that is what is meant by his statement: 'which is'; i.e., pure impugnment by fisq of the witness; i.e., he reveals the fisq of the witness. And it does not establish a right for the Shari'ah, like the obligation of a hadd penalty, or for a person, like the obligation of money. If it does establish, it is accepted, such as if they testify that the witness is impious, or consumes riba, or that he hired them, or a wine drinker at a time, or a fornicator at a time, or that he admitted that their testimony was false, or that the plaintiff is false in this case, or that they have no testimony against the defendant in this incident. And this testimony is not accepted because pure fisq is not subject to judicial ruling, and the judge has no means to enforce it. Evidence is only accepted for what is subject to judicial ruling and within the judge's power to enforce.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the ruling on 'jarh mujarrad' (pure impugnment) in testimony. The type is a definition with ruling. The passage begins by stating that testimony on pure impugnment is not accepted. It then provides examples: accusing a witness of being impious (fasiq), a consumer of riba, or hiring someone. The scenario is given: if the plaintiff brings evidence of a witness's integrity, and the opponent brings evidence to impugn that witness, if the impugnment is pure (i.e., does not establish a legal right), it is not considered. However, if the impugnment establishes a right (e.g., proof of a hadd penalty or financial obligation), it is accepted. The linguistic and technical definitions of jarh are provided: linguistically, it means to speak ill of someone; technically, it means revealing the fisq of a witness. The key distinction is whether the impugnment entails establishing a right of Allah (like hadd) or of a person (like financial rights). If it does, it is accepted; if it is pure (mujarrad), it is not. The reason is that pure fisq does not fall under the judge's jurisdiction; he cannot enforce a ruling based on it. Evidence is only accepted for matters that the judge can adjudicate and enforce. Examples of pure impugnment include saying 'he is fasiq', 'eats riba', etc. Examples of impugnment that establish a right include testimony that the witness committed zina (which can lead to hadd) or that he admitted false testimony (which can lead to liability).

Key Terms
الجرح المجرد (al-jarḥ al-mujarrad): Pure impugnment: showing the fisq (sinfulness) of a witness without that act entailing the establishment of a legal right for either Allah or a human.
الفسق (al-fisq): Sinfulness or impiety; a legal disqualifier for acceptable testimony. Here, it is used in the context of impugning a witness's integrity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is accepted only if the witness is a defendant.
D) It is accepted only in criminal cases.

Key Takeaway
Testimony that merely accuses a witness of sin without establishing an enforceable legal right is inadmissible as impugnment in Hanafi law.

The Non-Acceptance of Abstract Invalidation (Jarḥ Mujarrad) in Testimony
Defines abstract invalidation and explains its non-acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define abstract invalidation, distinguish it from non-abstract invalidation, and explain why the Hanafi school rejects abstract invalidation testimony, citing the reasoning that it is not subject to judicial enforcement.

Core Idea
Abstract invalidation testimony is rejected because it concerns sinfulness not subject to judicial enforcement.

In Hanafi law, not every allegation against a witness is accepted in court. This lesson explores the concept of 'abstract invalidation' (jarḥ mujarrad)—testimony that merely brands a witness as sinful without establishing a specific legal right. We will see why such testimony is inadmissible and how the school distinguishes it from invalidation that does create a legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
Define Abstract Invalidation
Identify the key characteristics: testifying that a witness is sinful without establishing a specific right for Allah or an individual. Examples: saying 'he is a sinner', 'he is a usurer', 'he hired them'.
The term 'jarh mujarrad' literally means 'abstract invalidation'.
2
State the Ruling
Recognize that such testimony is not accepted (ghayr maqbul) in the Hanafi school. The passage states: 'Evidence is only accepted upon what is subject to judicial ruling and within the judge's capacity to enforce it.'
3
Understand the Rationale
The reason is that abstract sinfulness is not subject to judicial enforcement; the judge cannot compel anything based on a general accusation of sinfulness. This is because the witness may have repented, and the testimony itself may involve spreading lewdness (which is prohibited).
Also, the testifier becomes a sinner by spreading lewdness.
4
Distinguish Non-Abstract Invalidation
Contrast with cases where invalidation does establish a specific right, e.g., admission by the plaintiff that the witnesses are sinful, or testimony that witnesses are slaves, had been flogged for slander, or are partners of the plaintiff. These are accepted because they involve matters the judge can enforce.
These examples are given in the passage.
5
Evaluate the Counterargument
Consider the objection based on the hadith 'Help your brother whether oppressor or oppressed'—arguing that accepting testimony prevents oppression. The response: There is no necessity because the opponent can inform the judge privately, so a less harmful alternative exists. Thus, the general principle (evidence only for enforceable matters) prevails.
This shows the use of istihsan (juristic preference) to avoid harm.

(1) ينظر: «التبيين» (٤: ٢٢٧). (۲) «المصباح المنير»(ص٩٥). As for sinfulness not being subject to judicial ruling, it is due to the possibility that he may have repented in his council before, so enforcement is not realized, and because the witness by this testimony becomes sinful; for it involves spreading lewdness, which is prohibited by text, and the matter testified to is not established by the testimony of a sinner. If you say: There is necessity in it, which is preventing the oppressor from oppression through false testimony, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Help your brother whether he is an oppressor or oppressed,' so it should not be permissible. We say: There is no necessity for this testimony because he can inform the judge secretly so that their testimony is rejected, so preventing oppression is possible by that. Contrary to when the invalidation is non-abstract, for testimony is accepted in it, as will come later, God willing. [1] His statement: 'I only said: the form...' etc.; it is said: There is consideration here, which is that the purpose is that such testimonies are not considered whether they are before the modification of the witnesses or after, so there is no need to mention the restricted forms. The answer: The meaning of considering invalidation testimony is the non-acceptance of testimony and judging thereby, and this meaning is realized before modification, not after, so restriction to after is necessary, as is not hidden.

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from a commentary on the matn of al-Wiqayah. The passage defines 'abstract invalidation' (jarh mujarrad) as testimony that declares a witness sinful without establishing a specific legal right for Allah (like a hadd penalty) or for an individual (like financial obligation). The ruling is that such testimony is not accepted. The reasoning is that abstract sinfulness is not a matter subject to judicial enforcement; the judge cannot compel anything based on it. Evidence is only accepted for matters that can be enforced. The passage provides examples of abstract invalidation: saying 'he is a sinner', 'he is a usurer', 'he hired them', etc. It also clarifies that if the invalidation entails a specific right (e.g., establishing that the witness is a slave or has been punished for qadhf), it is accepted. The commentator then addresses an objection: one might argue that there is a necessity to prevent false testimony, citing the hadith 'Help your brother whether oppressor or oppressed'. The response is that there is no necessity because the opponent can inform the judge privately, thus avoiding the need for public testimony. Finally, a super-commentator (hashiya) explains that the restriction of the ruling to cases where the plaintiff has already established the witnesses' uprightness is necessary because before modification, the testimony of invalidation is not needed; after modification, it becomes relevant.

Key Terms
الجرح المجرد (al-jarh al-mujarrad): The act of declaring a witness sinful without establishing a specific legal right for Allah or for an individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is abstract invalidation (jarh mujarrad) testimony not accepted in the Hanafi school?
A) Because it may be based on hearsay.
B) Because it does not involve a legal right that the judge can enforce.
C) Because it is always false.
D) Because the witness may repent.

Key Takeaway
Abstract invalidation testimony is rejected because it concerns sinfulness that is not subject to judicial enforcement; only invalidation establishing a legal right is accepted.

Acceptance of Testimony on Plaintiff's Admission of Witnesses' Defects
States that testimony based on plaintiff's admission of his witnesses' defects is accepted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that testimony based on the plaintiff's admission of his witnesses' defects is accepted, and explain the reasoning that iqrar is subject to judicial ruling.

Core Idea
The plaintiff's own admission of a witness's defect makes testimony admissible, because a judicial admission binds the admitter.

In this passage, the Hanafi school clarifies a specific rule regarding testimony: when the plaintiff himself admits that his witnesses are sinful or otherwise defective, that admission can form the basis for rejecting or questioning the testimony. This is because an admission (iqrar) is a matter that the judge can enforce, unlike a general claim of sinfulness. The passage also lists several examples of defects that, if admitted by the plaintiff, are accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that testimony is accepted (i.e., the judge can consider the plaintiff's admission as a basis to reject the witness).
2
List the types of defects
The passage lists: sinfulness, being slaves, those flogged for qadhf, wine-drinkers, slanderers, partners of the plaintiff, or hired by him.
These are examples; the principle applies to any defect admitted.
3
Locate the proof
The proof is given in the text: 'because admission is subject to judicial ruling.'
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli), not a text from Qur'an or Sunnah.
4
Understand the Hanafi principle
In Hanafi law, iqrar is a binding declaration that the judge can enforce, unlike abstract invalidation (which is not accepted).
Thus, the plaintiff's admission triggers a legal consequence.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
This ruling is mukhtalaf fih; other schools may not accept testimony on admission of sinfulness, but the Hanafi school does.

This is a ruling statement in the same chapter on testimony. It states that testimony is accepted when it is based on the plaintiff's own admission of his witnesses' sinfulness or other defects (like being slaves, having been punished for qadhf, being wine-drinkers, etc.). The reasoning is that an admission (iqrar) is a matter that comes under judicial ruling; the judge can enforce it. Unlike abstract invalidation, which is not accepted, testimony on admission is accepted because it involves a clear legal consequence. When is Testimony About Witness Disqualification Accepted? A Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on acceptance of testimony about witnesses' own disqualification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven specific cases where testimony about witness disqualification is accepted in Hanafi law, and explain the legal reasoning and the exception for mere sinfulness.

Core Idea
Testimony about a witness's sinfulness is not accepted, but testimony on admission, slavery, hadd, recent drinking, slander, partnership, or hired falsehood is admissible.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah' addresses a critical procedural question: when can a witness be disqualified based on someone else's testimony? The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between situations where the disqualification testimony itself becomes a legal act with binding effect (like an admission) versus mere slander. Understanding this ruling helps us grasp the Hanafi commitment to both procedural justice and protection of moral reputation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its cases
Read the first part of the passage listing where testimony about jarh is accepted. Note the seven scenarios: admission of fisq, slavery, hadd for qadhf, drinking wine (recent), slander (with claim), partnership, hiring.
The list is exhaustive for accepted testimony.
2
Examine the proof for acceptance in each case
For each scenario, identify the legal basis: iqrar is binding, slavery is a right of Allah, hadd is a judicial fact, etc.
The commentary justifies each briefly.
3
Analyze the exception for mere fisq
Why is testimony about sinfulness alone rejected? Two reasons: possibility of repentance before ruling, and the testifier becomes fasiq by spreading obscenity.
This is the key nuance.
4
Evaluate the objection and Hanafi response
The objection claims necessity to prevent false testimony based on the hadith 'Help your brother...'. The Hanafi response: no necessity because private informing suffices, so the hadith does not override the prohibition of spreading obscenity.
This shows the school's prioritization.
5
Distinguish jarh mujarrad from mudarraj
The text hints that if disqualification includes details, it may be accepted. Understand the difference: mere accusation vs. specific evidence.
This nuance is important for application.

And because the witnesses did not spread obscenity, but rather reported the spread of obscenity by others, so they do not become sinful, thus the testimony is established by it, so their testimony is accepted. And testimony is accepted that they are slaves, because slavery is a right of Allah the Exalted, and implicitly it establishes the ownership of the slave. Or that they are those who have been subjected to hadd punishment for slander, because the testimony does not involve spreading obscenity, as the disclosure was done by judiciary, and they only reported the disclosure of obscenity by others. Or drinkers of wine: and by that is meant that they testify that they drank wine, and the time has not passed, as it entails establishing a right of Allah the Exalted, which is the vinegar. But if it has passed, the testimony is not accepted due to lack of establishing the right by it, because testimony about a hadd punishment that has passed is rejected. Or slanderers: with the opening of the dhal (the dotted letter), plural of qadhib, meaning that they testify that they slandered so-and-so, on condition that the slandered person claims that, because in slander there are both the right of Allah and the right of the servant. Unlike if the slandered person does not claim it, for then no right is established. Or partners of the plaintiff: when the testimony concerns their partnership, and the claimed property is shared by them. The meaning is that the witness is a partner in absolute partnership, so whatever occurs in this [property] of falsehood, he has benefit in it, not that he is his partner in the claimed thing, otherwise it would be an admission that the claimed thing belongs to both. Thus in 'al-Fath' (1) and others. And the reason testimony is accepted in this form is their establishment of the right of partnership, and its detail is that disqualification in this manner, though it makes the witness sinful, it does not establish a right of Allah (peace be upon him) nor of the servant, because it does not establish the witnesses' right to partnership in that property, because when they testify to the property for the defendant, it is as if they admitted that they have no ownership in it. So by the testimony of the disqualification witnesses that they are partners of the plaintiff, nothing is established for them. Or that he, i.e., the plaintiff, hired them, i.e., the witnesses, for such-and-such dirhams, for it, i.e., for testimony, meaning to give false testimony, and gave them that mentioned amount of dirhams. From what I had with him; that establishes disqualification based on it. i.e., from my property that was in his hand, so the testimony is accepted because he is a contestant in
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah' explains when testimony (shahada) about the disqualification (jarh) of other witnesses is admissible. The base ruling is that testimony against witnesses is accepted in specific cases: when the plaintiff admits the witnesses are sinful (fasiq), or when the witnesses are slaves, or have received hadd punishment for qadhf (false accusation of zina), or are known drunkards, or are slanderers, or are partners of the plaintiff, or were hired for false testimony. The author justifies each. For example, admission of sinfulness falls under judicial power because it persists (repentance does not erase the legal effect before modification). Testimony about slavery establishes a right of Allah. Testimony about hadd punishments is accepted because it does not spread obscenity but reports a judicial fact. Testimony about drinking wine is accepted only if recent, because the right (becoming vinegar) must be provable. Testimony about being slanderers requires the slandered party to claim. Testimony about partnership is accepted because it prevents the witness from benefiting from falsehood. The text also addresses an objection: why not accept testimony of sinfulness to prevent injustice? The answer is that the judge can be informed in private, so there is no necessity to accept it publicly. The commentary also clarifies that the ruling applies only when the disqualification is not mere (mujarrad) but substantial.

Key Terms
فسق (fisq): Sinfulness; moral depravity that disqualifies a witness in Islamic law.
جرح (jarh): Legal disqualification of a witness; the act of impugning a witness's credibility.
إقرار (iqrar): Admission; a party's acknowledgment of a fact, which binds him judicially.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a scenario where testimony about witness disqualification is accepted according to the passage?
A) Testimony based on the plaintiff's admission that his witnesses are fasiq.
B) Testimony that witnesses are slaves.
C) Testimony that witnesses are slanderers (qadhif) without the slandered party's claim.
D) Testimony that witnesses are recent drinkers of wine.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school carefully restricts testimony about witness disqualification to cases where it establishes a legal fact or right, rejecting mere accusations of sinfulness to protect reputation and public morality.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

When Witness Testimony Is Accepted Despite Apparent Taint
Listing categories of witnesses whose testimony is accepted with legal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Ḥanafī principle for accepting testimony from witnesses with potential taint and apply it to determine acceptance in each listed category.

Core Idea
A witness's testimony is accepted if the taint does not create a claimable right for them or against them.

This passage from ʿUmdat al-Riʿāya presents several categories of witnesses whose testimony is accepted despite factors that might appear to disqualify them. The key is that the taint (jarḥ) does not establish a legal right (ḥaqq) that would make the witness a party in the case. By working through these examples, you will understand the nuanced reasoning of the Ḥanafī school on witness credibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching principle
The unifying rule is that testimony is accepted when the taint does not give the witness a personal claim or obligation that would make them an opponent in the case.
The passage repeatedly uses the phrase 'does not establish a right of Allah nor of the slave' to explain acceptance.
2
Analyze each category individually
For each of the six or more categories listed, note what the taint is and why it does not create a claimable right. For example, a partner testifying for the plaintiff is effectively admitting no personal ownership, so no right arises.
Check the distinction between recent and distant wine drinking; distant drinking does not establish a hadd right, so testimony is rejected.
3
Apply the test to borderline cases
For each category, ask: 'Does this taint give the witness a right to the property or impose a liability on them that would make them a litigant?' If no, testimony is accepted.
4
Note the exceptions and conditions
The passage explicitly states when testimony is rejected (e.g., distant hadd, unclaimed slander). These exceptions confirm the rule.

(۱) «فتح الغفار»(٦ : ٤٩٧). أي من مالي الذي كان في يده، فتقبل الشهادة ؛ لأنه خصم في كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها باب القبول وعدمه. أو إني صالحتهم على كذا، ودفعته إليهم على أن لا يشهدوا علي وشهدوا، ولو شهد عدل ولم يبرح مكانه حتَّى قال : أوهمت بعض شهادتي قبل أو إني صالحتهم على كذا ، ودفعته إليهم على أن لا يشهدوا علي وشهدوا) : أي على أن لا يشهدوا علي شهادة الزور، ومع ذلك شهدوا شهادة الزور، فيجب عليهم أداء ما أعطيتهم، فإنّ في هذه الصُّورِ يوجب الجرح حقاً للشرع أو العبد على الشهود، فيدخل تحت حكم القاضي فيقبل. [1] قوله : أو اني... الخ ؛ وكذا ادعى أجنبي أنه دفع بهم كذا ؛ لئلا يشهدوا على فلان بهذه الشهادة، وطلب ردّه ، وثبت إما ببينة أو إقرار أو نكول، فإنّه يثبت به فسقُ الشاهد، فلا تقبل شهادته. كذا في «البحر»
And because the witnesses did not manifest the indecency, but rather reported the manifestation of indecency by others, so they do not become sinful, thus the witnesses are established thereby and their testimony is accepted. Testimony is accepted that they are slaves, for slavery is a right of Allah Almighty, and within it is establishment of ownership for the slave. Or (witnesses) who have been punished for slander (qadhf); because the testimony does not contain spreading of indecency, because the manifestation occurred through the court, and they only reported the manifestation of indecency by others. Or drinkers of wine; and the meaning is that they testified that they drank wine, and the time is not distant, because therein is establishment of a right of Allah Almighty, which is the hadd (punishment). But if it is distant, their testimony is not accepted, due to lack of establishment of the right thereby; because testimony regarding a distant hadd is rejected. Or (witnesses) who are slanderers (qādhiƒūn) – with the dhāl pronounced with fatḥa – plural of qādhiƒ: meaning they testified that they slandered someone, on condition that the slandered person claims it, because in slander there is both a right of Allah and a right of the slave (individual) together, unlike if the slandered person does not claim it, for then no right is established thereby. Or partners of the plaintiff; in the case where the testimony pertains to their partnership, and the claimed property is shared among them, so the meaning is that the witness is a partner (sharik mufāwiḍ), so whatever occurs in this [property] of the falsehood, he has benefit in it; it is not meant that he is his partner in the claimed property, otherwise it would be an admission that the claimed property belongs to both. Such is stated in al-Fatḥ (1) and others. The reason testimony is accepted in this scenario is their establishment of the right of partnership, and its detail is that the taint (jarḥ) in this manner, although it makes the witness sinful, does not establish a right of Allah nor of the slave, because by their testimony for the property for the plaintiff, it is as if they admitted that they have no ownership in it, so by the testimony of the taint witnesses that they are partners of the plaintiff, nothing is established for them. Or that he – i.e., the plaintiff – hired them – i.e., the witnesses – for such and such amount of dirhams, for it – i.e., for the testimony, meaning to produce false testimony, and he gave them that mentioned amount of dirhams. from what was mine. with him. If an upright (ʿadl) witness has not left his place until he says: I made a mistake in part of my testimony, it is accepted. Or (the case) I made a settlement with them for such and such, and paid it to them on condition they would not testify against me, and (then) they testified: meaning on condition they would not testify falsely against me, yet they gave false testimony, so they must return what I gave them. For in these scenarios the taint establishes a right for the Sharīʿa or the slave against the witnesses, so it falls under the judge's jurisdiction and is accepted. [1] Commentary: His saying "Or that I..." etc.; similarly, if a third party claims that he paid them such and such so that they would not testify against so-and-so with this testimony, and demands its return, and it is established either by evidence or admission or refusal (nukūl), then the witness's sinfulness is established, so his testimony is not accepted. Such is stated in al-Baḥr.
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting several categories of witnesses whose testimony is accepted despite factors that might appear to taint their credibility. The overarching principle is that testimony is acceptable if the taint (jarḥ) does not establish a claimable right for Allah or for the litigants that would make the witness a self-interested party in the case. The author lists specific cases: (1) Witnesses who confess to having committed adultery themselves – they are not considered sinful because they did not manifest the indecency, only reported it, so their testimony is accepted. (2) Witnesses who have been punished for slander (qadhf) – their testimony is accepted because the punishment was by court order, not because they spread gossip. (3) Witnesses who admit to drinking wine – as long as the drinking is recent, because it establishes a hadd right for Allah; if too much time has passed, the hadd is not established and testimony is rejected. (4) Witnesses who are slanderers (qādhifūn) – they testify that they slandered someone, but the testimony is accepted only if the slandered party claims the right, since slander involves both Allah's and the victim's rights. (5) Witnesses who are partners of the plaintiff in the disputed property – their testimony is accepted because they are not establishing their own ownership; rather, by testifying for the plaintiff, they are implicitly admitting they have no share, so the taint does not create a conflict of interest. (6) Witnesses hired by the plaintiff to give false testimony – the hiring itself shows corruption, but if the plaintiff sues them for return of payment, they become opponents, so their testimony is accepted on that issue. (7) A witness who makes a settlement with the plaintiff not to testify, then testifies – this establishes a right to return of the payment, so the taint becomes a claimable right, thus within judicial purview. The hashya clarifies that if an outsider makes a similar payment claim, it also establishes the witnesses' sinfulness. The overall principle is that when the taint gives rise to a legal claim (ḥaqq) against the witness, the testimony on that claim is accepted because the witness is then a litigant.

Key Terms
جرح (jarḥ): A defect in a witness's credibility, such as sinfulness (fisq) or having a personal interest in the case.
محدودون في قذف (maḥdūdūn fī qadhf): Witnesses who have been subjected to the ḥadd punishment for false accusation of adultery (qadhf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the partner is considered the owner of the property along with the plaintiff.
B) Because the witness, by testifying for the plaintiff, is effectively admitting that he has no ownership in the property, so the taint does not create a personal right.
C) Because partnership makes the testimony stronger.
D) Because the witness is not legally competent to be disqualified.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is accepted when the taint does not create a claimable right that would make the witness a party in the case.

Witness Correcting Mistake Immediately After Testimony
Ruling on a witness who retracts part of testimony while still in the same sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a witness's immediate correction of testimony is accepted according to the Hanafi school and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
An upright witness may correct a mistake before leaving the court; otherwise, the original testimony stands.

In courtroom testimony, a witness may realize an error immediately after speaking. The Hanafi school addresses this situation with a clear ruling: the correction is accepted only if the witness is upright (ʿadl) and has not yet left the place. This lesson examines the exact conditions, the scope of 'mistake', and the rationale behind this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a witness correcting his testimony. The ruling is that it is accepted (maqbūl) under specific conditions.
2
Define the conditions
The witness must be ʿadl (upright) and must not have left his place (lam yabruḥ makānahu). The correction must be immediate, i.e., in the same sitting.
3
Understand the scope of mistake
The term 'awhamtu' includes doubt, error, forgetfulness. It must be a partial mistake ('in part of my testimony'), not a complete retraction.
If he says the right belongs to someone else, it is not accepted.
4
Identify the rationale
The rule is based on the possibility of error due to the awe of the courtroom. Immediate correction is trusted; after leaving, the witness may have time to fabricate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

As they have stated. [3] Commentary: His saying 'I made a mistake' (awhamtu) – or 'I doubted' or 'I erred' or 'I forgot'; such is in al-Miʿrāj. Wahimah fī al-ḥisāb yawhamu wahman, like ghalita ghalatan, in pattern and meaning; it is transitive by hamza and double letters, and sometimes the hamzated form is used intransitively. Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with accompanying commentary (hashya) that clarifies the conditions for accepting a witness's retraction or correction of his testimony while still in the courtroom. The ruling states that if an upright (ʿadl) witness, meaning one whose moral integrity is established, has not left the place of testifying (the court) and says 'I made a mistake (awhamtu) in part of my testimony,' then his statement is accepted and the testimony is considered corrected. The hashya explains key words: 'upright' (ʿadl) is specified because if the witness is not upright (e.g., a fāsiq), his testimony is categorically rejected regardless of whether he corrects himself or not. The term 'awhamtu' is explained to include doubt (shakk), error (ghalat), or forgetfulness (nisyān); it refers to a mistake in the testimony. The phrase 'part of my testimony' is understood as 'in part of my testimony,' and if the witness says the mistake is that the right belongs to someone else entirely, it is not accepted because that would be a complete retraction rather than a correction. The reasoning is that a witness may innocently make an error due to the intimidating atmosphere of the court, so immediate correction is allowed.

Key Terms
عدل (ʿadl): A witness who is morally upright and legally qualified to testify; his integrity is established.
أوهمت (awhamtu): I made a mistake, including doubt, error, or forgetfulness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) His correction is not accepted, and the original testimony stands.
C) It is accepted only if he returns to the courtroom.
D) It is accepted only if he provides proof of the mistake.

Key Takeaway
An upright witness may correct a mistake in his testimony only if he does so immediately before leaving the courtroom; otherwise, the original testimony stands.

Ruling on Payment to Witnesses to Avoid False Testimony
Ruling on payment to witnesses to avoid testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on payment to witnesses to avoid false testimony and explain the legal reasoning (talil) behind the return of payment.

Core Idea
Paying witnesses to avoid false testimony creates a contractual right; breach by false testimony obligates return.

In this passage, the commentator explains the ruling when someone pays witnesses on condition that they do not give false testimony, yet they give it. The key legal issue is whether such a payment creates a valid claim for return. Understanding this ruling requires parsing the distinction between a mere discrediting (jarh) and a claim that involves a right enforceable by the judge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the claim
The passage discusses a person who reconciles (sulh) with witnesses by paying them so that they do not testify falsely. When they do testify falsely, the payer demands his money back. State the claim: return of payment.
The condition must be specific: not to give false testimony.
2
Distinguish between jarh and a valid legal claim
The text says that without the claim of reconciliation, the matter would be mere jarh (discrediting), which alone is not enough for the judge to order return. The claim of reconciliation makes it a legal right.
Jarh affects testimony admissibility; claim affects financial obligation.
3
Understand the talil (reasoning) from al-Zayla'i
Al-Zayla'i explains that the claim is valid because it involves obligating return of property to a well-known person (al-mashhoor 'alayh), which falls under judicial authority.
4
Compare with the rejected analogy of hiring (isti'jar)
The text rejects the idea that this is like hiring because in hiring, the claimant is acting for someone else and lacks authority. Here, the payer claims for himself.
5
Apply the extended ruling from al-Bahr
Even a stranger who paid witnesses to avoid false testimony can demand return, and the witnesses' sin is proven, rejecting their testimony.
The principle extends beyond the original party.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو إني صالحتهم على كذا، ودفعته إليهم على أن لا يشهدوا علي وشهدوا) : أي على أن لا يشهدوا علي شهادة الزور، ومع ذلك شهدوا شهادة الزور، فيجب عليهم أداء ما أعطيتهم، فإنّ في هذه الصُّورِ يوجب الجرح حقاً للشرع أو العبد على الشهود، فيدخل تحت حكم القاضي فيقبل. وعلل الزَّيْلَعِي ) بقوله : لأنّ دعواه صحيحة، لما فيه من إيجاب رد المال على المشهور عليه، وهو مما يدخل تحت الحكم ، ولو لم يقله لا تقبل الشهادة ؛ لأنّ الدعوى غير صحيحة، فكان جرحاً مجرداً ؛ لأنه لم يدع قبله حـقـاً يمكن القضاء به، ودعوى الاستئجار وإن كانت صحيحة لكنّه يدعيها لغيره، وليس لـه ولاية إلزام غيره لغيره. انتهى. فظهر فائدة القيود.
[1] قوله : أو اني... الخ ؛ وكذا ادعى أجنبي أنه دفع بهم كذا ؛ لئلا يشهدوا على فلان بهذه الشهادة، وطلب ردّه ، وثبت إما ببينة أو إقرار أو نكول، فإنّه يثبت به فسقُ الشاهد، فلا تقبل شهادته. كذا في «البحر».
Or I reconciled with them for such-and-such, and paid them on condition that they not testify against me, and they testified. That is, on condition that they not give false testimony against me, yet they gave false testimony. So they must pay back what I gave them, because in these cases the cause of injury (jarh) creates a right for the Shari'ah or for the servant over the witnesses, so it falls under the judge's ruling and is accepted. And al-Zayla'i explained, saying: Because his claim is valid, since it involves obligating the return of property to the well-known person (al-mashhoor 'alayh), and that is something that falls under a legal ruling. And if he does not say it, the testimony is not accepted because the claim is not valid, so it is mere jarh (discrediting), since he did not claim a right that can be adjudicated. The claim of hiring (isti'jar) is valid, but he claims it for someone else, and he has no authority to obligate someone else for another. End. So the benefit of the conditions becomes apparent.
[1] His statement: 'Or I reconciled...' etc. Likewise, if a stranger claims he paid them such-and-such so that they would not testify against so-and-so with this testimony, and demands its return, and it is proven by evidence or admission or refusal (nukul), then the witness's sin is proven, so his testimony is not accepted. Thus in al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the matn discusses the ruling when someone pays witnesses to avoid testimony, particularly false testimony. The text states that if a person reconciles with witnesses by paying them not to testify (specifically not to give false testimony), and then the witnesses do testify falsely, they must return the payment. The reason is that their act of false testimony, despite the payment, establishes a cause for jarh (discrediting) which entitles the payer to a right—either a right of Allah or a personal right. This claim falls under the jurisdiction of the judge and thus the judge accepts the claim and orders the return of the money. Al-Zaylai explains that the claim is valid because it involves the return of property, which is a legal matter. If the payer does not make this claim, the testimony is not accepted because the claim is not valid and the jarh is mere discrediting without a basis for a legal ruling. The analogy of hiring (isti'jar) is rejected because in that case the claimant claims for someone else and lacks authority to obligate another. The footnote from al-Bahr adds that if a stranger (non-party) claims to have paid the witnesses, he can also demand return once proven, and the witnesses are deemed sinful and their testimony rejected.

Key Terms
الجرح (al-jarh): Discrediting or impugning the integrity of a witness, making their testimony unacceptable.
حق للشرع أو العبد (haqq li al-shar' aw al-'abd): A claim that is either a right of Allah (like prescribed penalties) or a personal right of an individual (like financial claims).
المشهور عليه (al-mashhoor 'alayh): The person against whom a claim is well-known; here, the person who is known to have paid the witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must the witnesses return the payment in the case where they were paid not to give false testimony?
A) Because the payment was a bribe for true testimony.
B) Because the claim of reconciliation creates a right to return the money when the condition is breached.
C) Because the judge always orders return of money in any case involving witnesses.
D) Because the payment was made under duress.

Key Takeaway
Payment to avoid false testimony creates a valid claim for return if the condition is breached.

Witness Correcting Error While Still in Court
Ruling on a righteous witness correcting error

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a witness's correction of testimony is accepted in the Hanafi school and apply them to scenarios involving error in amount or identity.

Core Idea
A righteous witness may correct an error only immediately in the same court session.

Testimony is a serious matter, but witnesses can err due to the awe of the court. The Hanafi school provides a clear rule: if the witness is righteous ('adl) and corrects the error before leaving the session, the correction is accepted. However, the conditions are nuanced — the type of error, the presence of suspicion, and the unity of the session all matter. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its key conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is a witness correcting his own testimony by saying 'I erred' (or similar) before leaving the court. The ruling is that this correction is accepted (yuqbal) under specific conditions.
The correction does not nullify the original testimony but amends it.
2
Check the Condition of 'Adalah (Righteousness)
The witness must be 'adl (righteous). If the witness is not 'adl (fasiq), his testimony is rejected absolutely, whether correction is made or not.
This restriction is explicitly mentioned in the text.
3
Examine the Requirement of Same Session
The correction must be made before the witness leaves the court (majlis). If made later, acceptance depends on whether there is suspicion of collusion (mawdi' shubhah).
If there is suspicion, later correction is rejected; if no suspicion, it may be accepted.
4
Understand the Proof (Dalil)
The ruling is based on qiyas: the witness may err due to the awe of the court, so immediate correction is analogous to retracting a statement before the session ends, which is permissible.
No explicit Quran or Hadith is cited; the dalil is rational (ma'qul).
5
Note the Intra-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
There is difference on whether judgment is given for the corrected amount or the original. Al-Sarakhsi prefers the corrected amount (e.g., if testified 1000 then says 500, judge for 500).
The mufta bihi is the preferred view of al-Sarakhsi.
