Contradictory Location Testimonies: Initial Rejection
Ruling on contradictory location testimonies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on contradictory location testimonies and explain the rational basis (dalīl 'aqlī) for rejecting both.

Core Idea
When two testimonies about the same act in different places are irreconcilable, both are rejected because one must be false.

In Hanafi evidence law, if two sets of witnesses give irreconcilable testimony about the location of a single event, the judge must reject both. This is not because either set is known to be lying, but because logical impossibility demands that at least one testimony is false. In this lesson, we examine the ruling and the rational proof behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its place
The act in question is the murder of Zayd, and the place is either Makkah or Kufa on the same day. Two witnesses say Makkah, two say Kufa.
The time and person are identical; only the location differs.
2
Recognize the contradiction
The two testimonies cannot both be true because a single event cannot occur in two different places simultaneously. Therefore, at least one set is false.
This is a contradiction in the testimony, not in the witnesses' character.
3
Apply the ruling of rejection
Since neither testimony is more credible than the other, both are rejected. The judge cannot prefer one over the other arbitrarily.
Rational certainty (yaqīn) that one is false leads to rejection of both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ولو شهدا بقتل زيد يوم كذا بمكة، وآخران بقتله فيه بكوفة ردتا) : أي شَهِدَ بقتل زيد في ذلك اليوم بكوفة ردت البينات ؛ لأنَّ أحدهما كاذبة بيقين"، وليست إحداهما أولى من الأخرى، فإن قضى بأحدهما ، ثُمَّ قامت الأخرى ردت هي) ؛ لأنَّ الأُولَى ترجّحت باتصال القضاء بها، فلا ينتقض بالثانية. 11 ] قوله : لأنَّ المدعي يكذب شاهد قضاء البعض ؛ وهو تفسيق له، فبقي واحد فلا تقبل ؛ لعدم كمال النصاب. [٤] [٢] قوله : قلنا : هذا إكذاب ...الخ ؛ وبيانه : إنَّ الشاهدين إذا شهدا لإنسان بمال ، ثم شهدا عليه بمال لإنسان آخر، فكذَّبهما المشهود عليه الذي هو مشهود له ، يقضى بما شهدا له، وإن كان يفسقهما فيما شهدا عليه ؛ لأنَّ هذا تفسيق عن اضطرار، والموجب للرد هو التفسيق عن اختيار. وكذلك لو شهد الشاهدان لرجل على رجل بألف درهم ومئة دينار، فكذَّبهما المشهود له في المئة الدينار تقبل شهادتهما ، ثمَّ هاهنا كذبـه فـيـمـا شـهـدا عـلـيـه وهـو القضاء، فلا يقدح في شهادته له. كذا في «الكفاية»(۲). [٣]قوله : كاذبة بيقين ؛ لأنّ الفعل الواحد وهو القتل لا يمكن أن يقع في مكانين. [٤]قوله : ترجحت...الخ ؛ لأنه لا حكم أنه قتل بمكة صار ذلك حكماً بأنه لم يقتل في غيرها ، إذ قتل شخص واحدٍ في مكانين لا يتصوّر، وهذا نظير مسألة التحري. (۱) قال الطحاوي في (مختصره) (ص٣٤٣): روي عن أبي يوسف له أنه قال : لا تقبل شهادة الشاهد الذي شهد على القضاء ؛ لأنه شهد على أن لا شيء للمدعي على المدعى عليه مما يطالبه به ، و به نأخذ. (۲) «الكفاية» (٦ : ٥٠٦).
And if two testify to the murder of Zayd on such a day in Makkah, and two others testify to his murder in Kufa on that day, they are both rejected. Then if a judgment is made by one of them, then the other is brought forward, it is rejected. This is based on the one who knows the judgment of part should not testify until the claimant confirms among the people what he has received, lest the defendant suffer harm. And al-Tahawi related from our companions that his testimony is not accepted, and it is the saying of Zufar, because the claimant discredits the witness of part of the judgment. We said: Discrediting in other than what is testified about does not prevent acceptance. (And if two testify to the murder of Zayd on such a day in Makkah, and two others testify to his murder in Kufa, they are both rejected): that is, they testified to the murder of Zayd on that day in Kufa, the evidences are rejected because one of them is certainly false, and neither is more deserving than the other. Then if judgment is made by one of them, then the other is brought forward, it is rejected because the first was strengthened by the continuity of the judgment with it, so it is not invalidated by the second. [2] His statement: Because the claimant discredits the witness of part of the judgment, and that is a declaration of his sinfulness, so only one remains and is not accepted due to the lack of complete number. [4] [2] His statement: We said this discrediting etc., and its clarification: That if two witnesses testify for a person for property, then testify against him for property for another person, and the one against whom they testify, who is the one for whom they testified, discredits them, judgment is made by what they testified for him, even if he declares them sinful regarding what they testified against him, because this is a declaration of sinfulness out of necessity, and the cause for rejection is declaration of sinfulness by choice. Similarly, if the two witnesses testify for a man against a man for a thousand dirhams and a hundred dinars, and the one for whom they testify discredits them regarding the hundred dinars, their testimony is accepted. Then here he discredits them regarding what they testified against him, and it is the judgment, so it does not impair their testimony for him. As in al-Kifayah. [3] His statement: Certainly false, because the single act, which is murder, cannot occur in two places. [4] His statement: Strengthened etc., because since it was ruled that he was killed in Makkah, that becomes a ruling that he was not killed elsewhere, since the killing of one person in two places is inconceivable, and this is similar to the issue of tahari (seeking the correct). (1) al-Tahawi said in his Mukhtasar: It is related from Abu Yusuf that he said: The testimony of the witness who testifies on the judgment is not accepted because he testifies that there is nothing owed by the defendant to the claimant from what he claims, and we take this. (2) al-Kifayah (6:506).
Source pages p. 592

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with commentary from a Hanafi fiqh work on contradictory testimonies regarding the location of a murder. The main ruling states: if two witnesses testify that the murder occurred in Makkah and two others testify it occurred in Kufa on the same day, both testimonies are rejected because they are irreconcilably contradictory—one must be false. However, if a judge already gave a verdict based on one testimony, and then the other is brought later, the second is rejected because the first has been given legal effect and cannot be overturned by mere contradiction. The commentary then addresses a related issue: a witness who knows of a previous judgment in a case should not testify until the claimant publicly acknowledges receipt, to avoid harm to the defendant. It cites al-Tahawi's report from the Hanafi school that such a witness's testimony is not accepted (the view of Zufar), because the claimant's discrediting of the witness regarding the prior judgment amounts to a tafsīq (declaration of sinfulness). The response from the author is that discrediting regarding something other than what is currently testified does not prevent acceptance—this is because discrediting is under duress due to the witness's testimony against the claimant, similar to a case where witnesses testify for a person and then against him in another matter: the discrediting does not invalidate the earlier testimony. The commentary also gives examples from al-Kifayah to illustrate the principle that forced tafsīq does not reject testimony. The passage concludes by analogizing to the issue of tahari (seeking the correct direction), where a prior valid effort is not invalidated by later doubt.

Key Terms
تكذيب (takdhīb): Discrediting or accusing a witness of lying.
تفسيق (tafsīq): Declaration that a witness is sinful (fāsiq), which may lead to rejection of testimony.
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony given in court by a witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are both testimonies about the location of the murder rejected initially?
A) Because the witnesses are known to be unreliable.
B) Because it is rationally impossible for the same murder to occur in two places, so one set must be false.
C) Because the judge must decide which testimony is more credible.
D) Because the claimant did not confirm the receipt.

Key Takeaway
Contradictory location testimonies are both rejected because logical certainty of falsity in one set makes it impossible to prefer either.

Shahadat — Testimony

Effect of Prior Discrediting on Witness Testimony
Sub-issue on prior discrediting and tafsīq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on accepting testimony when the claimant has discredited the witness in a prior proceeding, distinguishing forced tafsīq from voluntary tafsīq.

Core Idea
Discrediting a witness out of necessity does not make them sinful; only voluntary tafsīq rejects testimony.

In Hanafi law, a witness who previously testified for a claimant in a case that ended with a judgment may later testify for the same claimant in a different matter. If the claimant discredits the witness regarding the prior testimony—because it now harms his interest—does that disqualify the witness for the current testimony? The Hanafi school, contra Zufar and al-Tahawi, holds that such discrediting does not disqualify, because it is done under duress (idṭirār) and not by choice. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
A witness testified for a claimant in a prior case (e.g., confirming a payment), and judgment was given. Later, the same witness testifies for the same claimant in a new case. The claimant now discredits the witness regarding the prior testimony because it hurts his position.
The prior testimony was in the claimant's favor at that time.
2
Identify the opposing view
Zufar and al-Tahawi argue that by discrediting the witness, the claimant effectively declares the witness sinful (tafsīq), so only one witness remains (the other being discredited), and the required number (nisāb) is not met.
They consider the discrediting as voluntary.
3
Understand the Hanafi response
The majority (including the author) argue that this discrediting is not voluntary but necessary (idṭirār); the claimant is forced to discredit the witness to avoid a loss. Only voluntary tafsīq rejects testimony.
The key principle: 'al-ikdhāb fī ghayr al-mashhūd bihi lā yamna‘ al-qabūl' (discrediting about something other than the current testimony does not prevent acceptance).
4
Apply the principle
Confirmed by analogy: if witnesses testify for a person (for property) and later against him, the person's discrediting of them in the latter case does not invalidate their earlier favorable testimony. Similarly here.
The tafsīq is a consequence of the witness's new testimony, not a reflection of their character.

A) Because the discrediting is about a different matter and is not voluntary.

Difference in Testimony on Stolen Cow's Color or Gender
Intra-Hanafi dispute on admissibility of testimony with conflicting descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on conflicting testimonies about the color and gender of a stolen cow and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
When testimonies differ on the same object, reconciliation is key; but if the objects differ, the case collapses.

This passage from ‘Umdat al-Ri‘āya addresses a classic Hanafi procedural issue: when two witnesses testify to the theft of a cow but disagree on its description—color or gender. The ruling affects whether the hadd (amputation) is applied. The passage reveals an important intra-madhhab disagreement between Imām Abū Ḥanīfa and his two disciples, Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī (al-Ṣāḥibayn). Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi approach to reconciling testimonies and the strict evidentiary standards for ḥudūd punishments.

Guided Path
1
State the disagreement
Identify the two scenarios (color vs gender) and the divergence between Imam and Sahibayn.
Imam: amputation for color difference, not for gender. Sahibayn: no amputation in either case.
2
Examine Imam’s reasoning
Understand the possibility of reconciliation due to nighttime, distance, or a two-colored cow.
Imam argues that the witnesses may be describing the same animal perceptually differently.
3
Review Sahibayn’s objection
Objects are different → different thefts → insufficient testimony for a single act.
A white cow is not a black cow; thus the testimonies are not for the same act.
4
Consider the analogy to ghasb
If conflicting testimony fails in ghasb (easier to prove), it fails a fortiori in hadd.
Hadd is stricter; if ghasb is not established, hadd cannot be.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Sahibayn’s view is preferred because of the strictness of hadd and the need for caution.
Sadr al-Shari‘a said 'al-azhar qawluhumā' (the more apparent is the saying of the two).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شهدا بسرقة بقرة، واختلفا في لونها قطع ، ولو اختلفا في الذكورة لا (ولو شهدا بسرقة بقرة ، واختلفا في لونها قطع ، ولو اختلفا في الذكورة لا)، وعندهما" : لا يقطعُ في الوجهين ، وقيل : الاختلاف في لونين متشابهين كالسَّوادِ ، والحمرة لا في السَّوادِ والبياض. وقيل: في جميع الألوان، له: أن السرقة قد يقع في الليالي، والرائي يراه من بعيد، فاللونان يتشابهان ، والأظهر قولهما). [١]قوله : ولو شهدا...الخ ؛ يعني إنَّ الشاهدين إذا شهدا على سرقة بقرة، واختلفا في لونها ، فقال أحدهما : سرق بقرة بيضاء، وقال الآخر : بقرة سوداء، تقبل شهادتهما عند الإمام، فإذا قبلت قطع يد السارق وعندهما لا تقبل، فلا يقطع يد السارق ، ولو اختلفا في الذكورة والأنوثة، بأن قال أحدهما : سرق ذكراً، والآخر : سرق أنثى لا تقبل شهادتهما عند الإمام أيضاً. [٢) قوله : وعندهما...الخ ؛ هذا الخلاف فيما إذا كان المدعي يدعي سرقة بقرة مطلقاً من من غير تقييد بوصف، أما إذ ادَّعى سرقة بقرة سوداء أو بيضاء لا تقبل شهادتهما بالإجماع ؛ لأنَّ المدعي كذَّبَ أحدهما. [٣]قوله : لا يقطع في الوجهين ؛ لأنَّ البقرة البيضاء غير البقرة السوداء، فكانا سرقتين مختلفتين ، ولم تتم على فعل واحد نصاب الشهادة، فلم يثبت، صار كاختلافهما في الذكورة والأنوثة، وكاختلافهما في اللون في الغصب، بل أولى؛ لأنَّ الثابت بالغصب ضمان لا يسقط بالشبهات، والثابت بالسرقة حد، وهو يسقط. والحد أعسر إثباتاً من الغصب ؛ لأنَّ الغصب يثبت بشهادة النساء مع الرجال ، وبالشهادة على الشهادة، والحد ليس كذلك ، فلما لم يثبت الغصب بمثل هذه الشهادة ، فأولى أن لا يثبت الحد بها. [٤] قوله : له أن ...الخ ؛ تقريره : إنَّ التوفيق ممكن ؛ لأنَّ السرقة تكون في الليالي غالباً، ويكون التحمل فيها من بعيد، فيتشابه على الشاهدين اللونان، أو يجتمعان في بقرة، بأن كان أحد جانبيها أبيض. (۱) نقل الحصكفي في الدر المنتقى ( ۲ : ۲۰۸) و (الدر المختار (٤) : ٣٩٢ ترجيح الشارح فقال : قال صدر الشريعة : والأظهر قولهما.
And if two testify to the theft of a cow, and they differ on its color, amputation is carried out; and if they differ on its gender, no (amputation). (And if two testify to the theft of a cow, and they differ on its color, amputation is carried out; and if they differ on its gender, no (amputation)), and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): amputation is not carried out in either case. And it is said: the difference is in similar colors like black and red, not in black and white. And it is said: in all colors. For him (Imam): because theft may occur at night, and the viewer sees from a distance, so the two colors resemble each other. And the more apparent is the saying of the two (Sahibayn). [1] His statement: 'And if two testify...' means that when two witnesses testify to the theft of a cow and differ on its color, one says white, the other says black, their testimony is accepted according to Imam, so if accepted, the thief's hand is amputated; but according to the two, it is not accepted, so the hand is not amputated. If they differ on gender, one says male, the other says female, their testimony is not accepted according to Imam as well. [2] His statement: 'And according to the two...' this difference is when the claimant claims theft of a cow absolutely without specifying a description. But if he claims theft of a black or white cow, their testimony is not accepted by consensus because the claimant has discredited one of them. [3] His statement: 'Amputation is not carried out in either case' because a white cow is not a black cow, so they are two different thefts, and the required number of witnesses for a single act is not completed, so it is not established. It becomes like differing on gender, and like differing on color in the case of usurpation (ghasb), rather even more so, because what is established by usurpation is a guarantee (damān) that is not dropped by doubts, while what is established by theft is a hadd (fixed punishment) that is dropped by doubts. And the hadd is more difficult to prove than usurpation, because usurpation is established by testimony of women with men, and by testimony upon testimony, while the hadd is not. So when usurpation is not established by such testimony, it is even more so that the hadd is not established by it. [4] His statement: 'For him (Imam)...' its exposition: Reconciliation is possible because theft often occurs at night, and bearing testimony is from a distance, so the two colors appear similar to the witnesses, or they may be combined in one cow, such that one side is white and the other black. (1) Al-Haskafi quoted in al-Durr al-Muntaqa (2:208) and al-Durr al-Mukhtar (4:392) that the commentator (al-Sharif) said: Sadr al-Shari'a said: The more apparent is the saying of the two.
Source pages p. 593

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the admissibility of testimony when witnesses differ on the description of a stolen cow. The matn (base text) states: if two witnesses differ on the cow's color, amputation is carried out (according to Imam Abu Hanifa); if they differ on gender (male/female), no amputation. The commentary explains that according to Imam, testimony is accepted for color difference because the theft often happens at night and colors can be mistaken or the cow might have two colors, so reconciliation is possible. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that amputation is not carried out in either case because a white cow and a black cow are different objects, so the witnesses are testifying to different thefts, and the required complete number of witnesses (two) for one act is not achieved. They analogize to gender difference and to usurpation, arguing that if usurpation (which only results in a monetary guarantee) is not established by such conflicting testimony, then hadd (which is more strictly proven) should not be either. The commentary notes that this disagreement only applies when the claimant alleges theft of a cow without specifying color; if he specifies black or white, the testimony is rejected by consensus because the claimant discredits one witness. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Sahibayn, as stated by Sadr al-Shari'a: 'the more apparent is the saying of the two.' This is confirmed by later sources like al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Key Terms
الذكورة (al-dhukūra): Masculinity; referring to the gender of the stolen animal (male).
الحد (al-hadd): Fixed corporal punishment (here, amputation of hand for theft).
الغصب (al-ghasb): Usurpation; wrongful taking of property without force of theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in this passage, what is the ruling if two witnesses agree a cow was stolen but one says it was white and the other says black?
A) The thief's hand is amputated because the witnesses agree on the theft.
B) The thief's hand is not amputated because the testimonies are considered contradictory.
C) The case is referred to a higher judge for a ruling.
D) The witnesses are punished for false testimony.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, when witnesses differ on the identity or essential description of the stolen property, the hadd punishment is not applied, as per the preferred opinion of the Sahibayn.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Differing Witness Descriptions in Theft Cases
Intra-Hanafi dispute on acceptance of differing testimony on color/gender and price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab disagreement on accepting testimony when witnesses differ on the color or gender of a stolen cow, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A difference in description between witnesses may or may not invalidate testimony, depending on whether reconciliation is possible.

Witness testimony is the backbone of proof in Islamic criminal law. But what happens when two witnesses agree on the fact of theft but disagree on the description of the stolen property? Does their testimony still count? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this question, with Imam Abu Hanifa taking a more flexible position than his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view and identifies the relied-upon ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, recognize that there are three opinions within the Hanafi school: two from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and one from Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn say the hadd is not cut in either case. Imam Abu Hanifa says if the difference is in color, the hand is cut; if in gender, it is not cut.
The Sahibayn's view is considered the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
2
Understand the reasoning of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn argue that a white cow is not a black cow, so the witnesses are actually testifying about two different thefts. The minimum number of witnesses for a single act (nisab al-shahada) is not met, so the hadd cannot be applied. They also draw an analogy to usurpation (ghasb), where even financial liability is not established with such testimony, and hadd is harder to prove.
Their reasoning relies on the objective impossibility of reconciling the two descriptions.
3
Understand the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that reconciliation (tawfiq) is possible: theft often occurs at night and from a distance, making colors appear similar, or the cow may have two colors. Thus, the witnesses are describing the same incident, and the testimony is valid, leading to the hadd penalty.
He distinguishes between color (reconcilable) and gender (not reconcilable).
4
Contrast with the sale/kitaba example
The passage extends the same principle to contracts: if witnesses differ on the price in a sale, the testimony is generally rejected because the contract changes with the price. However, if reconciliation is possible (e.g., the price was later increased), some accept it. This shows the consistent application of the reconciliation principle.
In the sale example, the majority view rejects testimony because the price is essential to the contract.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its significance
The commentator (sadr al-Shari'ah) states 'al-azhar qawluhuma' (the more apparent is the view of the two disciples). Therefore, in practice, the hand is not cut in either case. This ruling is relied upon for fatwa.
The tarjih is based on the principle that hadd is waived by doubts (shubhat).

ولو شهدا بسرقة بقرة، واختلفا في لونها قطع، ولو اختلفا في الذكورة لا (ولو شهدا بسرقة بقرة، واختلفا في لونها قطع، ولو اختلفا في الذكورة لا)، وعندهما: لا يقطعُ في الوجهين، وقيل: الاختلاف في لونين متشابهين كالسَّوادِ، والحمرة لا في السَّوادِ والبياض. وقيل: في جميع الألوان، له: أن السرقة قد يقع في الليالي، والرائي يراه من بعيد، فاللونان يتشابهان، والأظهر قولهما). [١]قوله: ولو شهدا...الخ؛ يعني إنَّ الشاهدين إذا شهدا على سرقة بقرة، واختلفا في لونها، فقال أحدهما: سرق بقرة بيضاء، وقال الآخر: بقرة سوداء، تقبل شهادتهما عند الإمام، فإذا قبلت قطع يد السارق وعندهما لا تقبل، فلا يقطع يد السارق، ولو اختلفا في الذكورة والأنوثة، بأن قال أحدهما: سرق ذكراً، والآخر: سرق أنثى لا تقبل شهادتهما عند الإمام أيضاً. [٢) قوله: وعندهما...الخ؛ هذا الخلاف فيما إذا كان المدعي يدعي سرقة بقرة مطلقاً من غير تقييد بوصف، أما إذ ادَّعى سرقة بقرة سوداء أو بيضاء لا تقبل شهادتهما بالإجماع؛ لأنَّ المدعي كذَّبَ أحدهما.
[٣]قوله: لا يقطع في الوجهين؛ لأنَّ البقرة البيضاء غير البقرة السوداء، فكانا سرقتين مختلفتين، ولم تتم على فعل واحد نصاب الشهادة، فلم يثبت، صار كاختلافهما في الذكورة والأنوثة، وكاختلافهما في اللون في الغصب، بل أولى؛ لأنَّ الثابت بالغصب ضمان لا يسقط بالشبهات، والثابت بالسرقة حد، وهو يسقط. والحد أعسر إثباتاً من الغصب؛ لأنَّ الغصب يثبت بشهادة النساء مع الرجال، وبالشهادة على الشهادة، والحد ليس كذلك، فلما لم يثبت الغصب بمثل هذه الشهادة، فأولى أن لا يثبت الحد بها.
[٤] قوله: له أن ...الخ؛ تقريره: إنَّ التوفيق ممكن؛ لأنَّ السرقة تكون في الليالي غالباً، ويكون التحمل فيها من بعيد، فيتشابه على الشاهدين اللونان، أو يجتمعان في بقرة، بأن كان أحد جانبيها أبيض والجانب الآخر أسود، فيشهد كل بما رأى أو بما وقع عنده، بخلاف وصف الذكورة والأنوثة؛ لأنهما لا يجتمعان في بقرةٍ واحدة، وكذا الوقوف على تلك الصفة يكون بالقرب، فلا يشتبه، فيكونان سرقتين مختلفتين، فلم يتم في كل واحدٍ منهما نصاب الشهادة. وبخلاف الغصب؛ لأنَّ التحمَّل فيه بالنهار على قرب منه، فإنَّ الغصب يكون غالباً في النهار، وهاهنا مباحث نفيسة، تركناها خشيةً عن التطويل، ولعل الشارح قال: والأظهر قولهما؛ نظراً إلى تلك المباحث.
[١]قوله: ولو شهد...الخ؛ صورته: إنَّ زيداً اشترى عبداً من عمرو بألف وخمسمئة دراهم، وأنكر أحدهما، فشهد أحد الشاهدين أنَّ زيداً اشترى ذلك العبد من عمرو بألف، وشهد الآخر أنه اشترى بألف وخمسمئة، فلا تقبل شهادتهما؛ لأنَّ المقصود من دعوى البيع قبل التسليم هو إثباتُ السبب، وهو العقد. والظاهرُ أنَّ البيع بألف غيرُ البيع بألف وخمسمئة، فاختلف المشهود به باختلاف الثمن، فلم يتم النصاب على واحد منهما. وذكر علاء الدين السَّمَرْ قَنْدِي له: إنَّ الشهادة تقبل؛ لأنَّ التوفيق ممكن، فإنَّ الشراء الواحد قد يكون بألف ثمَّ يصيرُ بألف وخمسمئة بأن يشتريه بألف ثم يزيده عليه خمسمئة، فقد اتفقا على شراء واحد. ولو اختلفا في الجنس بأن شهدَ أحدهما أنه اشتراه بألف درهم، وشهد الآخر أنه اشتراه بمئة دينار بطلت؛ لعدم إمكان التوفيق؛ لأنَّ الشراء الواحد لا يتصور أن يكون بألف درهم ثم يصير بمئة دينار. كذا في «التبيين» وكذلك الكتابة، فإنَّ عقد الكتابة يختلف باختلاف البدل، فإنَّ المقصود هو العقد، وذلك ظاهر إذا كان المُدَّعى هو العبد، فإنَّ العقد مقصوده، فلا تقبل الشهادة
Book of Testimony and Retraction Thereof: Disagreement in Testimony. And if two witnesses testify to the theft of a cow and differ on its color, [the hand] is cut; and if they differ on its gender, not [cut]. (And if two witnesses testify to the theft of a cow and differ on its color, [the hand] is cut; and if they differ on its gender, not [cut]), and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the hand is not cut in either case. And it is said: the difference is between similar colors like black and red, not between black and white. And it is said: in all colors. For him (Abu Hanifa): that theft often occurs at night, and the observer sees it from afar, so the two colors resemble each other, and the more apparent is their (the two disciples') view. [1] His statement: 'and if two witnesses testify... etc.' means that when two witnesses testify to the theft of a cow and differ on its color, one saying he stole a white cow and the other a black cow, their testimony is accepted according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). If accepted, the hand of the thief is cut. According to them (the two disciples), it is not accepted, so the hand is not cut. And if they differ on gender (male or female), such that one says he stole a male and the other a female, their testimony is not accepted according to the Imam either. [2] His statement: 'and according to them... etc.' This disagreement is when the plaintiff claims theft of a cow absolutely without specifying an attribute. But if he claimed theft of a black or white cow, their testimony is not accepted by consensus, because the plaintiff has belied one of them. [3] His statement: 'the hand is not cut in either case' because a white cow is not a black cow, so they are two different thefts, and the minimum number of witnesses (nisab) for one act is not complete, so it is not established. It becomes like their disagreement on gender (male/female), and like their disagreement on color in usurpation (ghasb), indeed even more so, because what is established by usurpation is liability (daman) which is not dropped by doubts, while what is established by theft is the hadd penalty, which is dropped by doubts. And the hadd is harder to establish than usurpation, because usurpation is established by the testimony of women along with men, and by testimony on testimony, whereas the hadd is not like that. So when usurpation is not established by such testimony, it is more appropriate that the hadd not be established by it. [4] His statement: 'for him... etc.' Its explanation: reconciliation is possible because theft often occurs at night, and bearing witness takes place from afar, so the two colors appear similar to the witnesses, or they can be combined in one cow, e.g., one side white and the other side black, so each witnesses what he saw or what occurred to him. Unlike the description of maleness and femaleness, because they cannot be combined in one cow, and also ascertaining that attribute is done up close, so it is not ambiguous. Thus they become two different thefts, and the complete quorum of testimony is not met in each one. And unlike usurpation, because bearing witness to it occurs by day and at close range, since usurpation usually occurs in the daytime. And here there are valuable investigations which we have omitted for fear of prolixity, and perhaps the commentator said 'and the more apparent is their view' in view of those investigations. [1] His statement: 'and if two witnesses testify... etc.' Its scenario: Zayd bought a slave from Amr for one thousand five hundred dirhams, and one of them denied it. Then one witness testified that Zayd bought that slave from Amr for one thousand, and the other testified that he bought it for one thousand five hundred. Their testimony is not accepted, because the purpose of the claim of sale before delivery is to establish the cause (sabab), which is the contract. And apparently, a sale for one thousand is not a sale for one thousand five hundred, so the matter testified to differs with the difference in price. Thus the quorum (nisab) is not complete for either one. And ‘Ala’ al-Din al-Samarqandi mentioned for him (Abu Hanifa?) that the testimony is accepted because reconciliation is possible, for a single purchase may be for one thousand then become one thousand five hundred, by buying it for one thousand then increasing it by five hundred. So they agreed on a single purchase. And if they differed in type (jins), e.g., one testified that he bought it for one thousand dirhams and the other for one hundred dinars, it is invalidated because reconciliation is impossible, for a single purchase cannot be conceived as being for one thousand dirhams then becoming one hundred dinars. Such is in 'al-Tabyeen'. And similarly for kitaba (contract of manumission by payment), for the kitaba contract differs with the difference in the substitute (badal), because the purpose is the contract, and that is clear when the claimant is the slave, for the contract is his purpose. So the testimony is not accepted.
Source pages p. 593

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the acceptance of testimony when witnesses differ on the description of the stolen property. The main issue is whether the hadd penalty of cutting the hand applies when two witnesses agree on the fact of theft but disagree on the color or gender of the stolen cow. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that if they differ on color, the hand is cut, because reconciliation is possible—the cow might have been seen from afar at night, or it could have two colors. However, if they differ on gender, the hand is not cut because a cow cannot be both male and female, so reconciliation is impossible. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that the hand is not cut in either case, because the difference in description indicates they are testifying to two different incidents, so the required number of witnesses for a single theft is not met. The commentary explains that this disagreement applies only when the plaintiff does not specify a color; if he claims a specific color, then the testimony is rejected by consensus because the plaintiff's claim contradicts one witness. The passage also extends this principle to sale and kitaba contracts. If two witnesses differ on the price in a sale, the testimony is rejected because the contract is defined by its price, and a sale for different amounts are different contracts. However, if reconciliation is possible (e.g., the price was later increased), some scholars accept the testimony. The relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) in the school is that of the Sahibayn, as stated by the commentator: 'the more apparent is their view.'

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given by witnesses to establish a claim or prove a crime.
قطع (qat'): Cutting of the hand as the hadd penalty for theft.
توفيق (tawfiq): Reconciliation or harmonization of seemingly conflicting witnesses' statements.
نصاب الشهادة (nisab al-shahada): The minimum number of witnesses required for proof; typically two males for hudud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, if two witnesses testify that a cow was stolen but one says it was white and the other says black, what is the ruling on the hadd penalty?
A) The hand of the thief is cut because reconciliation is possible.
B) The hand is not cut because the witnesses differ on an essential attribute.
C) The hand is cut only if the cow was white.
D) The testimony is accepted and the hand is cut, but only if the owner described the cow as multi-colored.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school regarding differing testimony on a stolen cow is that the hadd is not applied, regardless of whether the difference is in color or gender.

Shahadat — Testimony

Differing Testimony on Contract Price: Rulings and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on testimony when witnesses differ on price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when witnesses differ on the price in contracts and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected if witnesses differ on the price because the contract is defined by its price.

When two witnesses testify about a sale but disagree on the exact price, does their testimony count? In Hanafi fiqh, the price is an essential element of the contract; a sale for one thousand is not the same as a sale for one thousand one hundred. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the nuanced ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, including the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the initial statement: testimony is rejected (ruddat shahadatuhuma) when one witness says 1000 and the other says 1100. Note that this applies to sale, kitaba, and other contracts.
2
Understand the rationale
Follow the reasoning: each witness testifies to a different contract because the price differs. Thus each gives only shahadat fard (single witness testimony), and the required two witnesses are not met.
Compare with the example of describing an animal's gender, which is not essential to the contract.
3
Distinguish from other cases
See how the author contrasts with theft (where witnesses may differ on time/place) and usurpation (where conditions allow a single witness). Note the distinctions.
These distinctions reinforce the principle that price is integral to the contract.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi argued acceptance because reconciliation is possible (price increase later). The commentator indicates the preferred view (azhar) is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, rejecting Samarqandi's view.
The text mentions 'valuable investigations' that support the companions' position.
5
Apply to other contracts and the debt-like exception
The ruling extends to kitaba, 'itq bi mal, sulh, rahn, and khula'. However, when the other party (e.g., master, pledgee) claims, Abu Hanifa allows acceptance if witnesses differ verbally but agree in meaning, provided the plaintiff claims the greater. Note the refutation of this analogy to debt claims.
The mufta bihi is the view of the two companions, rejecting the testimony in all such cases.

ولو شهدَ بشراء عبد ، أو كتابته بألف ، والآخرُ بألف ومئة ردت شهادتهما) ، سواءٌ ادعى البائع أو المشتري ؛ لأنَّ العقد يختلف باختلافِ الثَّمن ، فيكون على كل واحدٍ شهادة فردٍ فلا تُقْبَل والجانب الآخرُ أسود، فيشهد كل بما رأى أو بما وقع عنده، بخلاف وصف الذكورة والأنوثة ؛ لأنهما لا يجتمعان في بقرةٍ واحدة، وكذا الوقوف على تلك الصفة يكون بالقرب، فلا يشتبه، فيكونان سرقتين مختلفتين، فلم يتم في كل واحدٍ منهما نصاب الشهادة. وبخلاف الغصب ؛ لأنَّ التحمَّل فيه بالنهار على قرب منه ، فإنَّ الغصب يكون غالباً في النهار، وهاهنا مباحث نفيسة، تركناها خشيةً عن التطويل، ولعل الشارح قال : والأظهر قولهما ؛ نظراً إلى تلك المباحث.
[١]قوله: ولو شهد...الخ ؛ صورته : إنَّ زيداً اشترى عبداً مـن عمـرو بـألـف وخمسمئة دراهم، وأنكر أحدهما ، فشهد أحد الشاهدين أنَّ زيداً اشترى ذلك العبد من عمرو بألف ، وشهد الآخر أنه اشترى بألف وخمسمئة ، فلا تقبل شهادتهما ؛ لأنَّ المقصود من دعوى البيع قبل التسليم هو إثباتُ السبب، وهو ا العقد. والظاهرُ أنَّ البيع بألف غيرُ البيع بألف وخمسمئة ، فاختلف المشهود به باختلاف الثمن، فلم يتم النصاب على واحد منهما. وذكر علاء الدين السَّمَرْ قَنْدِي له : إنَّ الشهادة تقبل ؛ لأنَّ التوفيق ممكن، فإنَّ الشراء الواحد قد يكون بألف ثمَّ يصيرُ بألف وخمسمئة بأن يشتريه بألف ثم يزيده عليه خمسمئة ، فقد اتفقا على شراء واحد. ولو اختلفا في الجنس بأن شهدَ أحدهما أنه اشتراه بألف درهم، وشهد الآخر أنه اشتراه بمئة دينار بطلت ؛ لعدم إمكان التوفيق ؛ لأنَّ الشراء الواحد لا يتصور أن يكون بألف درهم ثم يصير بمئة دينار. كذا في «التبيين» وكذلك الكتابة، فإنَّ عقد الكتابة يختلف باختلاف البدل، فإنَّ المقصود هو العقد، وذلك ظاهر إذا كان المُدَّعى هو العبد، فإنَّ العقد مقصوده، فلا تقبل الشهادة
وكذا عتق بمال، وصلح عن قود، ورهن، وخلع، إن ادعى العبد، والقاتل، والراهن، والعرس، وإن ادعى الآخر، فهو كدعوى الدين في وجوهها (وكذا عتق بمال ، وصلح عن قود، ورهن، وخلع، إن ادعى العبد، والقاتل، والراهن، والعرس)، فيه لف ونشر، فدعوى العبد يرجع إلى العتق بمال، وهكذا على الترتيب، لأنَّ المقصود هنا هذا العقد وهو مختلف.
(وإن ادعى الآخر) : أي المولى في العتقِ على المال، وولي المقتول في الصلح عن القود، والمُرْتَهِنُ في الرَّهْن ، والزوج في الخلع ، (فهـو كـدعـوى الـديـن في وجوهها) : أي إن كان الشَّاهدان مختلفين لفظاً لا تقبل عند أبي حنيفة له وإن كانا متفقين معنى، فإن ادعى المدعي الأقل لا تُقْبَلُ شهادة الشاهد بالأكثر ، وإن ادعى الأكثر تقبل على الأقل. ولقائل أن يقول : ليس هذا كدعوى الدين ؛ لأنَّ الدين يثبت بإقـرار المديون، فيمكن أن يُقرَّ عند أحدِ الشَّاهدين بألف ، وعند الآخر بأكثر، ويمكن أيضاً أن يكون أصل الحقِّ هو الأكثر لكنَّه قَضَى الزَّائِدَ على الألف، أو أبرأ عنه عند أحد الشاهدين دون الآخر، فالتَّوفيقُ بينهما ممكن ، أمَّا هاهنا فالمالُ يثبت بتبعية العقدِ إذا اختلف الشاهدان في بدل الكتابة، وأما إذا كان المدَّعي هو المولى ؛ فلان مقصود الولي هو العتق ، وهو لا يثبت قبل الأداء، وهو لا يتحقق بدون الكتابة، فصارت هي مقصوده.
[1] قوله : وكذا...الخ ؛ أي لا تقبل الشهادة ؛ لأنَّ مقصود العبد، أو القاتل، أو الراهن، أو العرس إثبات العقد، والحاجة ماسة إليه، وثبوت العتاق والعفو والرهن والطلاق يبنى عليه.
وقال في «الهداية»(۱): وفي الراهن إن كان المدعي هو الراهن لا يقبل ؛ لأنه لا حظ له في الرهن، فعريت الشهادة عن الدعوى، وان كان هو المرتهن فهو بمنزلة الدعوى بالدين. انتهى.
[٢]قوله : ولقائل أن يقول ... الخ ؛ هذا نقض على قوله : فهو كدعوى الدين في
If one testifies to the purchase of a slave or his kitaba for one thousand, and another for one thousand one hundred, their testimony is rejected, whether the seller or buyer claims it; because the contract varies with the price, so each gives the testimony of a single witness and it is not accepted. The other side is black (unknown), so each testifies to what he saw or what occurred in his presence, unlike the description of male and female because they do not coexist in one cow, and similarly standing on that description is by nearness so there is no confusion, thus they are two different thefts and the full number of witnesses is not completed for either. And unlike usurpation because the taking occurs in the daytime from nearness, for usurpation usually occurs in the daytime. Here there are valuable investigations which we left out for fear of length. Perhaps the commentator said: the apparent view is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) considering those investigations.
[1] His statement: 'And if he testifies...' etc.; its illustration: Zayd bought a slave from Amr for one thousand five hundred dirhams, and one of them denied. Then one witness testified that Zayd bought that slave from Amr for one thousand, and the other testified that he bought for one thousand five hundred. So their testimony is not accepted because the purpose of the claim of sale before delivery is to establish the cause, which is the contract. And it is apparent that the sale for one thousand is different from the sale for one thousand five hundred, so the matter testified to differs with the price, thus the full number is not completed for either. And 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi opined that the testimony is accepted because reconciliation is possible: a single purchase could be for one thousand and then become one thousand five hundred if he buys it for one thousand and then increases five hundred. So they agree on one purchase. If they differed in kind, e.g., one witnessed that he bought it for one thousand dirhams, and the other for one hundred dinars, it is invalid because reconciliation is impossible since a single purchase cannot be for one thousand dirhams and then become one hundred dinars. Thus in al-Tabyin. Similarly kitaba, because the contract of kitaba varies with the substitute; the purpose is the contract. That is apparent when the claimant is the slave, for the contract is his purpose, so the testimony is not accepted.
And similarly emancipation for money, reconciliation for blood money, pledge, and khula' when the slave, the killer, the pledgor, or the wife claims. And if the other party claims, it is like a claim of debt in its aspects. (And similarly emancipation for money, reconciliation for blood money, pledge, and khula' when the slave, the killer, the pledgor, or the wife claims) there is order and reversal; the claim of the slave refers to emancipation for money, and so on in order, because here the purpose is this contract and it differs. (And if the other party claims) i.e., the master in emancipation for money, the guardian of the slain in reconciliation for blood money, the pledgee in pledge, and the husband in khula', (it is like a claim of debt in its aspects): i.e., if the two witnesses differ verbally it is not accepted according to Abu Hanifa, even if they agree in meaning. If the claimant claims the lesser, the testimony of the witness for the greater is not accepted; if he claims the greater, it is accepted for the lesser. And one may object: this is not like a claim of debt because a debt is proven by the admission of the debtor, so it is possible that he admitted one thousand before one witness and more before the other, and it is also possible that the original right was the greater but he paid the excess or remitted it before one witness and not the other, so reconciliation is possible. But here, the money is proven as a consequence of the contract when the two witnesses differ about the substitute in kitaba. And if the claimant is the master, then the purpose of the guardian is emancipation, which is not proven before payment, and cannot be realized without kitaba, so it becomes his purpose.
[1] His statement: 'And similarly...' etc.; i.e., the testimony is not accepted because the purpose of the slave, killer, pledgor, or wife is to establish the contract, and the need for it is pressing, and the establishment of emancipation, pardon, pledge, and divorce depends on it.
And it is stated in al-Hidayah: Regarding the pledge, if the claimant is the pledgor it is not accepted because he has no benefit in the pledge, so the testimony becomes devoid of a claim; but if it is the pledgee, it is like a claim for debt. End.
[2] His statement: 'And one may object...' etc.; this is a refutation of his statement: 'it is like a claim of debt in'
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage is from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah. It addresses the issue of testimony when two witnesses differ on the price or consideration in various contracts. The ruling is that if one witness testifies to a price of one thousand and another to one thousand one hundred in a purchase or kitaba, the testimony is rejected entirely. This is because the contract is defined by its price; a sale for one thousand is legally different from a sale for one thousand one hundred. Thus each witness gives only isolated testimony (shahadat fard), and the required number of witnesses is not met. This applies whether the plaintiff is buyer or seller. The author distinguishes this from cases like describing an animal's gender (where the witnesses agree on the fact of purchase but disagree on a non-essential attribute) and from theft and usurpation. A notable intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned: 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi argued acceptance of testimony because reconciliation is possible—the price could have been increased later. The commentator indicates the preferred view is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Qawlani: 'al-azhar qawlahuma'), rejecting Samarqandi's view. The passage then extends the ruling to other contracts: 'itq bi mal, sulh 'an qisas, rahn, and khula'. If the claimant is the party seeking to establish the contract (slave, killer, pledgor, wife), testimony is rejected due to differing consideration. If the claimant is the other party (master, guardian, pledgee, husband), the ruling follows that of debt claims in some aspects: according to Abu Hanifa, if witnesses differ verbally but not in meaning, the testimony is not accepted when the plaintiff claims the lesser, but is accepted for the lesser if he claims the greater. However, a refutation is given: debt claims are based on admission, allowing reconciliation; here the money is subsidiary to the contract, which itself differs, so reconciliation is not possible. The Hidayah is quoted for the specific ruling on rahn: if the pledgor claims, testimony is invalid because he has no interest in the pledge; if the pledgee claims, it is like a debt claim.

Key Terms
شهادة فرد (shahadat fard): Testimony of a single witness (less than two) which is not sufficient to prove a claim in Hudud and other cases.
كتابة (kitaba): A contract whereby a slave purchases his freedom by paying installments to the master.
عتق بمال ('itq bi mal): Emancipation of a slave in exchange for money, a type of contract.
صلح عن قود (sulh 'an qisas): Settlement in lieu of qisas (retaliation), e.g., accepting blood money (diyah) instead of execution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a case where two witnesses testify about a purchase: one says the price was 1000 dirhams, the other says 1100 dirhams. What is the ruling according to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the text?
A) The testimony is accepted if the plaintiff is the buyer.
B) The testimony is rejected because the price differs.
C) The testimony is accepted if the plaintiff is the seller.
D) The testimony is accepted only if the witnesses agree on the meaning.

Key Takeaway
When witnesses differ on the price in a contract, their testimony is rejected because each testifies to a different contract; the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the unconditional rejection of such testimony.

Shahadat — Testimony
advanced
10 min
The Ruling on Differing Witnesses in Contracts: The Analogy to Debt Claims
Ruling with proof via qiyas and response to objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on differing witnesses in four specific contracts (emancipation for price, settlement for qisas, pledge, and khul') and distinguish when testimony is rejected versus treated like a debt claim.

Core Idea
When witnesses differ in wording, the key is which party is claiming: the contract-seeker loses, but the money-seeker gets debt treatment.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya addresses a nuanced issue in testimony law: when two witnesses give different accounts regarding contracts like emancipation for a price, settlement for qisas, pledge, and khul'. The ruling depends crucially on whether the claimant is trying to prove the contract itself (like a slave claiming emancipation) or just the monetary obligation (like a master claiming payment). The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, draws an analogy to debt claims to resolve the latter case, but not without objections. In this lesson, you will learn the precise ruling, the underlying qiyas, and the response to a key objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four contracts and the parties involved
The passage lists emancipation for a price (al-‘itq bi māl), settlement for qisas (al-ṣulḥ ‘an al-qawad), pledge (al-rahn), and khul‘ (divorce by redemption). The parties are: slave/master, killer/guardian, pledgor/pledgee, husband/wife (or wife/husband depending on who claims).
Lubb wa nashr: the first set of claimants (slave, killer, pledgor, husband) correspond to the first set of contracts.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios: claimant seeking the contract vs. claimant seeking the money
If the claimant is the party whose primary goal is to establish the contract (e.g., slave seeking to prove emancipation, pledgor seeking to prove the pledge), then testimony is scrutinized strictly. If the claimant is the party seeking only the monetary compensation (e.g., master claiming payment, pledgee claiming debt), the ruling shifts to be like a debt claim.
In the first scenario, the contract is the main purpose; in the second, the money is the main purpose.
3
Apply the ruling for the contract-seeker: testimony rejected if witnesses differ in wording
When the slave, killer, pledgor, or husband claims the contract, and the two witnesses differ in wording (even if they agree in meaning), the testimony is not accepted. This is because the contract cannot be established through inconsistent testimony; each witness essentially provides a single testimony, making the total insufficient (needing two witnesses on the same fact).
The text says 'la tuqbal al-shahada' (testimony not accepted).
4
Apply the analogy to debt for the money-seeker: same ruling as debt claims
When the master (claiming money for emancipation), the guardian (claiming compensation for qisas), the pledgee (claiming the debt secured by the pledge), or the husband (claiming the khul' payment) brings witnesses, the ruling is like a claim of debt (dain). At Abu Hanifa: if witnesses differ in wording, testimony is rejected; if they agree in meaning, the plaintiff's claim determines acceptance (if claiming lesser, witness to greater not accepted; if claiming greater, witness to lesser is accepted).
This is the core qiyas: the primary object is the money.
5
Analyze the objection and the Hanafi response
An objector argues that the analogy to debt is flawed because in debt, reconciliation of differing testimonies is possible via the debtor's acknowledgment of payment or release, whereas in contracts the money is subsidiary and cannot be separated. The Hanafi response: (1) The contract itself is acknowledged by the plaintiff, so only the money needs proof, thus it reverts to a debt claim; (2) The comparison is only in the specific rulings on wording and agreement, not in all aspects.
Ponder both answers as the commentary suggests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة والرجوع عنها الاختلاف في الشهادة
وكذا عتق بمال، وصلح عن قود، ورهن، وخلع، إن ادعى العبد، والقاتل، والراهن، والعرس، وإن ادعى الآخر، فهو كدعوى الدين في وجوهها (وكذا عتق بمال ، وصلح عن قود، ورهن، وخلع، إن ادعى العبد، والقاتل، والراهن، والعرس)، فيه لف ونشر، فدعوى العبد يرجع إلى العتق بمال، وهكذا على الترتيب، لأنَّ المقصود هنا هذا العقد وهو مختلف.
(وإن ادعى الآخر) : أي المولى في العتقِ على المال، وولي المقتول في الصلح عن القود، والمُرْتَهِنُ في الرَّهْن ، والزوج في الخلع ، (فهـو كـدعـوى الـديـن في وجوهها) : أي إن كان الشَّاهدان مختلفين لفظاً لا تقبل عند أبي حنيفة له وإن كانا متفقين معنى، فإن ادعى المدعي الأقل لا تُقْبَلُ شهادة الشاهد بالأكثر ، وإن ادعى الأكثر تقبل على الأقل. ولقائل أن يقول : ليس هذا كدعوى الدين ؛ لأنَّ الدين يثبت بإقـرار المديون، فيمكن أن يُقرَّ عند أحدِ الشَّاهدين بألف ، وعند الآخر بأكثر، ويمكن أيضاً أن يكون أصل الحقِّ هو الأكثر لكنَّه قَضَى الزَّائِدَ على الألف، أو أبرأ عنه عند أحد الشاهدين دون الآخر، فالتَّوفيقُ بينهما ممكن ، أمَّا هاهنا فالمالُ يثبت بتبعية العقدِ إذا اختلف الشاهدان في بدل الكتابة، وأما إذا كان المدَّعي هو المولى ؛ فلان مقصود الولي هو العتق ، وهو لا يثبت قبل الأداء، وهو لا يتحقق بدون الكتابة، فصارت هي مقصوده.
[1] قوله : وكذا...الخ ؛ أي لا تقبل الشهادة ؛ لأنَّ مقصود العبد، أو القاتل، أو الراهن، أو العرس إثبات العقد، والحاجة ماسة إليه، وثبوت العتاق والعفو والرهن والطلاق يبنى عليه.
وقال في «الهداية»(۱): وفي الراهن إن كان المدعي هو الراهن لا يقبل ؛ لأنه لا حظ له في الرهن، فعريت الشهادة عن الدعوى، وان كان هو المرتهن فهو بمنزلة الدعوى بالدين. انتهى.
[٢]قوله : ولقائل أن يقول ... الخ ؛ هذا نقض على قوله : فهو كدعوى الدين في وجوهها، وقد يجاب عنه بأنَّ العقد كالخلع والعتق مثلاً يثبت بإقرار المدعي فلا يحتاجُ في إثباته إلى البينة، حتى يقال : إنَّ العقد بألف غير العقد بالأكثر ، وعلى كل واحد شهادةً فرد فلا تقبل، بل إنما يحتاج إليها ؛ لإثباتِ الدَّين، فصار كما إذا ذكر الشاهد الشيئين أحدهما غير محتاج إليه فيرجع حقيقة إلى دعوى الدين. ويمكن التوفيق هاهنا أيضاً، بأن يقر المدعي عليه بالعقـد علـى ألف عند شاهد وعند آخر بالعقد على أكثر، ويكون قد أبرأ المدعي المدعى عليه عن البعض أو قبضه عند شاهد والآخر عنه غافل. وقد يجاب عنه : بأنَّ المشبه لا يجب أن يكون في حكم المشبه به بجميع الوجوه، بل المراد بكونه كدعوى الدين أنَّ الشَّاهدين إذا كانا مختلفين لفظاً لا يقبلُ عند الإمام، وإن كانا متفقين فإن ادَّعى المدعي الأقل لا تقبل شهادة الشاهد من الأكثر، وإن ادعى الأكثر تقبل على الأقل، فتأمل في كلا الجوابين.
[١]قوله : والإجارة كالبيع في أوّل المدة ؛ يعني إذا كانت الدعوى في الإجارة في أول المدَّةِ قبل استيفاء المعقود عليه، واختلف الشاهدان لا تقبل كما لا تقبل عند الاختلاف في البيع ؛ للحاجة إلى إثبات العقد، سواء ادعى المؤجر أو المستأجر، وسواء كانت الدعوى بأقل المالين أو أكثرهما. وكالدين بعدها أي بعد المدة، فثبت ما اتفق عليه الشاهدان، وهو الأقل.
(۱) والجواب عن اعتراض الشارح : بأن المال في الصور الأربع وإن كان ثابتاً بالعقد حين العقد وتابعاً له لكن الأمر صار بالعكس حين الدعوى ؛ لأن صاحب الحق اعترف بالعقد والعتق والطلاق ؛ أي كان المال متبوعاً والعقد تابعاً عند الدعوى يعني المال مقصود تبعاً للقصد حين العقد ومقصود أصالة حين الدعوى، فالعقد مقصود تبعاً للمال ينظر: «درر الحكام (٢ : ٢٨٦) ، و(الشرنبلالية (۲) : ٣٨٦) ، و(حاشية الخادمي (ص٤٣٤)، وغيرهم.
Book of Testimony and Retraction Therefrom: Difference in Testimony. And likewise [testimony for] emancipation for a price, settlement in lieu of retaliatory killing (qisas), pledge (rahn), and khul' (divorce by redemption). If the slave, the killer, the pledgor, or the husband claims [the contract], [testimony is not accepted because the purpose is to prove the contract]. And if the other party claims [the money], it is like a claim of debt in its aspects. There is [in the text] lubb wa nashr: the claim of the slave refers to emancipation for a price, and so on in sequence, because the intended purpose here is this contract, and it is disputed. (And if the other claims): i.e., the master in emancipation for a price, the guardian of the slain in settlement for qisas, the pledgee in rahn, and the husband in khul'; (it is like a claim of debt in its aspects): i.e., if the two witnesses differ in wording, it is not accepted according to Abu Hanifa for him, even if they agree in meaning. And if the plaintiff claims the lesser, the testimony of the witness [who testifies] to the greater is not accepted; and if he claims the greater, it is accepted for the lesser. And someone may say: this is not like a claim of debt because debt is established by the debtor's acknowledgement; thus it is possible that he acknowledged [the debt] before one witness as a thousand and before another as more, and it is also possible that the original right was the greater but he paid the excess over a thousand, or he released [the debtor] from it before one witness but not the other; so reconciliation between them is possible. As for here, the money is established by following the contract if the witnesses differ on the consideration (badal) of the kitabah. And if the plaintiff is the master, then the guardian's purpose is emancipation, and it is not established before payment, and it is not realized without the kitabah, so it becomes his intended purpose. [1] His saying: 'And likewise...' etc.; i.e., testimony is not accepted because the purpose of the slave, the killer, the pledgor, or the husband is to prove the contract, and the need is great for it, and the establishment of emancipation, waiver, pledge, and divorce is built upon it. And he said in al-Hidayah: Regarding the pledgor (rahin), if the plaintiff is the pledgor, it is not accepted because he has no interest in the pledge, so the testimony is devoid of a claim; and if it is the pledgee, it is like a claim of debt. End. [2] His saying: 'And someone may say...' etc.; this is an objection to his saying 'it is like a claim of debt in its aspects.' And it may be answered about it that the contract, like khul' and emancipation, is established by the acknowledgement of the plaintiff, so there is no need for evidence to establish it; so it cannot be said that the contract for a thousand is different from the contract for more, and on each one there is a single testimony, so it is not accepted. Rather, evidence is needed only to establish the debt, so it becomes as if the witness mentioned two things, one of which is not needed, so in reality it reverts to a claim of debt. And reconciliation is possible here too: that the defendant acknowledges the contract for a thousand before one witness and before another the contract for more, and the plaintiff may have released the defendant from some [of the amount] or may have received it before one witness while the other was unaware of it. And it may also be answered that the compared thing (al-mushabbah) does not have to be in the ruling of the thing compared to (al-mushabbah bihi) in all aspects; rather, the meaning of it being like a claim of debt is that if the two witnesses differ in wording, it is not accepted according to the Imam, and if they agree [in meaning] and the plaintiff claims the lesser, the testimony of the witness to the greater is not accepted, and if he claims the greater, it is accepted for the lesser. So ponder both answers. [1] His saying: 'And hire (ijarah) is like sale at the beginning of the term and like debt after it'; meaning if the claim in ijarah is at the beginning of the term before the contracted object has been received, and the two witnesses differ, it is not accepted just as it is not accepted when they differ in sale due to the need to prove the contract, whether the lessor or lessee claims, and whether the claim is for the lesser or greater of the two amounts. And [it is] like debt after it, i.e., after the term, so what the two witnesses agree upon is established, which is the lesser. (1) The answer to the commentator's objection: that the money in the four cases, although it was established by the contract at the time of the contract and was subsidiary to it, the matter becomes reversed at the time of the claim: because the right-holder acknowledges the contract, emancipation, and divorce; i.e., the money was followed and the contract was subsidiary at the time of the claim, meaning the money was an intended purpose as subsidiary to the intention at the time of the contract, and it is an original intended purpose at the time of the claim. So the contract is intended as subsidiary to the money. See: Durar al-Hukkam (2:286), al-Shurunbulaliyya (2:386), Hashiyat al-Khadimi (p.434), and others.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqaya, discusses the ruling on when witnesses differ in their testimony regarding certain contracts: emancipation for a price, settlement for qisas, pledge, and khul'. The passage uses a literary device (lubb wa nashr) to correlate the four contracts with the four parties claiming them. The core principle: if the party seeking to prove the contract (e.g., the slave claiming emancipation) brings witnesses who differ in wording, their testimony is not accepted because the primary purpose is to establish the contract, not the money. However, if the other party (e.g., the master claiming the money) brings differing witnesses, the ruling is analogous to a debt claim: at Abu Hanifa, if witnesses differ in wording, testimony is rejected even if they agree in meaning; if they agree in meaning, the testimony is examined based on what the plaintiff claims. The passage then addresses an objection: the analogy to debt is imperfect because in debt cases, reconciliation of differing testimonies is possible through acknowledgment of payment or release, whereas in contract cases the money is subsidiary to the contract. The commentator offers two responses: (1) The contract itself can be acknowledged by the plaintiff, so the need for evidence is only for the money, and (2) the comparison to debt is only in the sense that if witnesses differ in wording, it is not accepted; if they agree in meaning, the ruling follows the same pattern. The passage also covers ijarah (hire): at the beginning of the term, it is like sale (testimony differing not accepted); after the term, it is like a debt claim (testimony accepted on the agreed amount, the lesser). The final footnote clarifies the reversal of intention: at contract formation, money is subsidiary to the contract; at claim, money becomes the primary intended object, and the contract is subsidiary. The Hanafi position is presented with Abu Hanifa's view highlighted.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahāda): Testimony given by witnesses in court to establish a claim or right.
الاختلاف في الشهادة (al-ikhtilāf fī al-shahāda): The situation where two witnesses provide different wordings or amounts in their testimony regarding the same claim.
العِتق (al-‘itq): Emancipation of a slave, either voluntarily or for a price (kitabah).
الصلح عن القود (al-ṣulḥ ‘an al-qawad): Settlement in lieu of retaliatory killing (qisas), typically where the family of the victim accepts monetary compensation instead of execution.
الرهن (al-rahn): Pledge or mortgage: giving an asset as security for a debt.
الخلع (al-khul‘): Divorce by redemption where the wife pays consideration to the husband to obtain divorce.
الكتابة (al-kitāba): The contract of kitabah (manumission by payment) where a slave agrees to pay his master a sum in installments for emancipation.
الإجارة (al-ijāra): Hire or lease: a contract for the use of an asset or services in exchange for rent/wages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a master (mawla) claims money from his slave for emancipation, and two witnesses differ in wording (one says 1000, the other says 1500), what is the ruling on their testimony at Abu Hanifa?
A) Accepted because the master is claiming money, like a debt claim.
B) Rejected because the witnesses differ in wording, even if the meaning is the same.
C) Accepted only if the master claims the lesser amount.
D) Rejected because the contract is the primary purpose.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of differing testimony in contracts hinges on whether the claim is for the contract itself or the monetary obligation, with the latter treated like a debt claim.

Testimony in Ijarah: Analogy to Sale and Debt
Commentary on ruling regarding testimony in ijarah compared to sale and debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on accepting testimony in ijarah when witnesses disagree on the amount and explain the qiyas to sale at the beginning and to debt after the term.

Core Idea
Ijarah testimony mirrors sale at start (contract focus) and debt after (payment focus).

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah clarifies the nuanced ruling regarding contradicting witnesses in ijarah contracts. The key distinction depends on the stage of the lease: before the term, the contract itself is the primary object; after, it is the unpaid wage. You'll learn how this triggers different analogies and why the Hanafi school adopts this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two temporal phases
Recognize that the ruling changes based on whether the dispute arises at the beginning of the lease term or after it has ended. At the beginning, the contract is the focus; after, the payment is the focus.
This distinction is crucial for applying the correct analogy.
2
Understand the qiyas to sale
At the beginning of the term, ijarah is analogized to a sale contract. In a sale, if witnesses disagree on the price, testimony is not accepted because the contract itself is disputed. Similarly, in ijarah, disagreement on the rental amount at the start indicates a dispute over the contract, so testimony is invalid.
The 'illa (effective cause) is that the primary object is the contract.
3
Understand the qiyas to debt
After the term has ended, the claim is about unpaid wages, so ijarah is analogized to a debt. In a debt claim, if witnesses agree on an amount, that amount is established. Thus, if two witnesses agree on a rental amount, only the lesser amount they both confirm is accepted.
If witnesses differ in wording, testimony is not accepted even after the term.
4
Apply the mufta bihi rule
According to Imam Abu Hanifa (mufta bihi), if the two witnesses differ in wording (e.g., one says '1000' the other says '1200'), the testimony is rejected entirely. If they agree on the same amount, then the plaintiff's claim determines: if he claims the lesser, both testimonies are accepted for that amount; if he claims the greater, only the lesser is established.
This rule applies regardless of the temporal stage, but the stage influences the initial analogy.

Source Text

Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from the matn regarding testimony in ijarah (hire) contracts when witnesses disagree on the amount. The ruling states that ijarah is treated like sale at the beginning of the term: because the primary object of the contract is the contract itself, if witnesses disagree on the rental amount, their testimony is not accepted, as in a sale where disagreement invalidates the testimony. However, after the term, ijarah is treated like a debt: the claim is for the wage owed, so the testimony is accepted for the amount both witnesses agree upon (the lesser). The commentary then addresses objections: one objection is that the contract itself can be proven by admission, so disagreement on amount should not matter, but the response is that the contract for one thousand is different from the contract for more, so each witness gives a single testimony that cannot combine with the other. Another reconciliation is that the defendant might have admitted to different amounts before different witnesses, and the plaintiff may have discharged part of the debt. Ultimately, the accepted view (mufta bihi) is that if witnesses differ in wording, testimony is rejected; if they agree, the plaintiff's claim determines which testimony is accepted. The commentary emphasizes that this is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijarah): A contract of hire or lease where one party provides benefit in exchange for payment.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given by a witness in court to establish a claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because ijarah is always like debt, and debt requires exact agreement.
B) Because at the beginning, the primary object is the contract itself, and disagreement means the contract is not proven.
C) Because the lessor can always admit the contract, so testimony is unnecessary.
D) Because the witnesses must be unanimous on the amount for any testimony to be accepted.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of testimony in ijarah hinges on whether the dispute concerns the contract itself (at term start) or the payment (after term), analogized to sale and debt respectively.

Testimony in Nikah: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas on Mahr Disagreement
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony in marriage when witnesses disagree on mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa's istihsan overrides the qiyas analogy to sale when witnesses disagree on mahr, and state the mufta bihi position for fatwa.

Core Idea
In nikah, mahr is subsidiary to the contract; disagreement on a subsidiary does not invalidate the origin by istihsan.

When two witnesses in a marriage contract disagree on the amount of mahr, does the testimony become invalid as in sale? Imam Abu Hanifa says no—by istihsan, the marriage is valid with the lower amount. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn).

Guided Path
1
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
The matn states: 'The marriage is valid for one thousand by istihsan, and they said: it is also rejected.' Determine who holds each position and what the practical difference is.
Imam Abu Hanifa: marriage valid with lower mahr. Sahibayn: testimony rejected entirely.
2
Analyze the qiyas supporting Sahibayn
The commentary explains: Sahibayn analogize marriage to sale. In sale, if witnesses disagree on the price, the testimony is invalid. Since both parties intend the contract, the same should apply to nikah. Trace this analogy.
The shared effective cause ('illa) is that both are contracts where the object (price/mahr) is essential.
3
Examine the istihsan of Imam Abu Hanifa
Imam departs from qiyas through istihsan: mahr is subsidiary (tabi') to marriage. Marriages are valid without specifying mahr, so disagreement on a subsidiary does not affect the primary contract. Verify this by noting that the origin (nikah) is agreed upon.
The subsidiary status is proven by the rule that nikah is valid without mahr at the time of contract.
4
Apply the ruling to the scenario
When witnesses agree on the marriage but disagree on mahr, the court 'judges by the lesser amount' due to their agreement on that part. State the outcome under Abu Hanifa's view.
The marriage stands with mahr equal to the lower amount (e.g., 1000 if one says 1000 and the other 1500).
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The commentary sides with Imam Abu Hanifa, citing Al-Hidayah and Al-'Inayah. Conclude that the relied-upon view for fatwa is Abu Hanifa's istihsan.
The Sahibayn's view is acknowledged but not operative.

Book of testimony and retraction thereof: Disagreement in testimony. And the marriage is valid for one thousand by istihsan, and they two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is also rejected. (And the marriage is valid for one thousand by istihsan, and they said: it is also rejected), this is the analogy (qiyas); because the intended object is the contract from both sides, so it becomes like sale. The aspect of istihsan: that property in marriage is subsidiary, and there is no disagreement regarding what is the origin, which is the contract, so it is established, then disagreement occurs in the subsidiary, so judgment is given for the lesser, and it is equal whether the claim is for the lesser of the two amounts. [1] His statement: 'And the marriage is valid for one thousand' means with the lesser of the two amounts by istihsan, and it is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa, whether the claim is from the husband or the wife, and whether he claims the lesser or the greater. [2] His statement: 'because...' etc.; this is the proof for qiyas, and its explanation is that the intended object from both sides is to establish the cause (sabab). Apparently, marriage for one thousand is not marriage for one thousand five hundred, so the testimony is invalid as in sale. By the admission of one of them, unlike manumission for property and khul' and sulh for intentional homicide, where the claim is of debt when the plaintiff is the husband, master, or guardian; because by his admission, qisas is dropped, and divorce and manumission occur, so only the claim of property separated from the cause remains. [3] His statement: 'The aspect of istihsan: that property...' etc.; its exposition: property in marriage is subsidiary; because of this, marriage is valid without specifying the mahr, and disagreement in the subsidiary does not necessitate disagreement in the origin if it is established. And the origin in marriage is halal status, union, and ownership of the vulva (buda'), because the legality of marriage is for that, and the obligation of mahr is to preserve the dignity from being treated lightly by allowing access without compensation, as established in its place. And there is no disagreement regarding what is the origin, then when disagreement occurs in the subsidiary, judgment is given for the lesser due to their agreement upon it. So stated in Al-Hidayah and Al-'Inayah.
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding testimony in marriage (nikah) when two witnesses disagree on the amount of mahr. The matn states that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the marriage is valid with the lower amount by istihsan, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions, Sahibayn) say the testimony is rejected entirely. The commentary first presents the qiyas (analogy) supporting the Sahibayn: marriage is like sale because both parties intend the contract, so if witnesses disagree on the price (mahr), the testimony should be rejected as in sale. Then, the istihsan of Imam Abu Hanifa is explained: property (mahr) in marriage is subsidiary (tabi') to the primary aim of marriage, which is the establishment of a lawful relationship. Since mahr is not an essential pillar (marriage is valid without specifying mahr), disagreement on the mahr does not affect the validity of the contract. The contract (marriage) is the origin, and it is established; the disagreement is only in the subsidiary (mahr), so judgment is given for the lesser amount that both witnesses agree upon. The commentary also distinguishes marriage from other contracts like manumission for property, khul', and sulh, where the claim is for debt because the primary object is property. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Imam Abu Hanifa's view due to the strength of istihsan. The passage emphasizes that this applies whether the plaintiff is the husband or wife and whether they claim the lesser or greater amount.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A juristic preference that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) due to a stronger evidence or consideration of public interest.
القَياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction: extending the ruling of an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause ('illa).
التبع (al-tabi'): Subsidiary or secondary element; in nikah, mahr is a subsidiary to the main purpose of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa accept testimony in marriage when witnesses disagree on the mahr, contrary to the analogy with sale?
A) Because marriage is more important than sale, so rules are relaxed.
B) Because mahr is a subsidiary element in marriage, and disagreement on a subsidiary does not invalidate the primary contract.
C) Because in marriage, witnesses are not required to agree on specific terms.
D) Because the Sahibayn's view is based on a weak hadith.

Key Takeaway
In nikah, mahr is subsidiary; disagreement on it does not invalidate the marriage contract, and the lesser amount is binding by istihsan.

The Requirement of Al-Jarr in Inheritance Testimony
States the ruling on requiring linking in inheritance testimony and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi requirement of al-jarr in inheritance testimony and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad from Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A witness must explicitly link property to the heir; simply stating it belonged to the deceased is insufficient.

This passage addresses a critical procedural rule in inheritance litigation: the requirement of explicit linking (al-jarr) in testimony. Without such linking, the heir's claim fails. The Hanafi school holds that the heir's ownership is newly established, requiring clear transfer, though Imam Abu Yusuf dissents. We will examine the reasoned arguments on both sides.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: the witness must say 'He died and left it as inheritance for him' or equivalent; otherwise testimony is rejected.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Imam Abu Yusuf does not require explicit linking; he accepts testimony that merely states the property belonged to the deceased.
Abu Yusuf's view is a valid intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Follow Abu Yusuf's proof
Understand his reasoning: inheritance is a succession, so the heir steps into the deceased's shoes; testimony for the deceased effectively testifies for the heir.
He cites examples like return for defect and defect claims passing to the heir.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Study the majority's argument: the heir's ownership is renewed in specific properties, not continuous; evidence includes istibra' for inherited slave-girl and charity rules.
Renewal requires explicit transfer; istishab does not suffice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if witnesses only say 'This was his father's', Abu Hanifa and Muhammad reject the testimony, while Abu Yusuf accepts it.
The mufta bihi is the majority view requiring jarr.
