الإمام قلد شريحاً له ، وهو تابعي، وتقليد التابعي لا يراه الإمام. قلت : منشأ الدليل احتجاج بإجماع الصحابة ؛ لأنَّ شريحاً لله كان قاضياً في زمن الصحابة، ومثل هذا التشهير لا يخفى على الصحابة، ولم ينكر عليه أحد منهم، فحل محل الإجماع، على أن شريحاً ، وإن كان تابعياً لكن الصحابة له سوغوا له في الاجتهاد، ورجعوا إلى قوله في المناظرة.
فمن كان بهذه المثابة من أئمة التابعين فحكمه حكم الصحابة له، حتى روي عن الإمام أنه يقلدهم وعد منهم فقال مثل مسروق ، والحسن، وعلقمة، وشريح ، ومن كان في رتبتهم فيكون في الحقيقة على هذا تقليد للصَّحابة ؛ لتجويزهم فعلهم وقولهم، لا سيما شريح له ، فإنّه كان قاضياً زمان عمر الله، ومن بعده من الخلفاء، فيكون فعله مشهوراً بينهم، فكيف لا يكون وهو بمحضر منهم، فيكون تقليده تقليداً

[٢]قوله : فيبعثه...الخ ؛ قال في «الهداية» (۳) : ثم تفسير التشهير منقول عن شريح ه ، فإنّه كان يبعثه إلى سوقه إن كان سوقياً، وإلى قومه إن كان غير سوقي بعد العصر
Section on perjury. Whoever confesses that he testified falsely is publicly disgraced and not punished corporally. [Commentary:] This is the beginning of the rulings of the perjurious witness, and they are mentioned last because truth is the foundation. The description of the issue: Whoever confesses to himself that he lied deliberately, saying 'I lied in what I testified intentionally,' the judge punishes him by disgracing him in the market if he is a market person, or to his people if he is not a market person at their gathering. Likewise, whoever testifies that a man was killed, then the beneficiary comes alive, so his lie is established with certainty. Shaykh al-Islam added that he testifies that someone died and then comes alive, but there is consideration; because it is possible that he relied in this testimony on the report of a reliable person, then the opposite becomes clear, and thus it does not appear that he testified falsely, unlike testimony of killing. But if he says 'I made a mistake', or 'I forgot', or 'I erred', or his testimony is rejected due to suspicion or discrepancy between the testimony and the claim or between the two testimonies, then he is not punished; because we do not know who among them is the liar—the beneficiary or the two witnesses or one of them, and the plaintiff may lie to attribute lying to the witness, and it cannot be proven by evidence because it is a matter of negation, and evidence is proof for affirmation. But if he confesses against himself, his confession is accepted, and its consequence of compensation and punishment is obligatory. Men, women, and dhimmis are equal in this matter, as stated by al-Zayla'i and others. Imam al-Hakim Abu Muhammad al-Katib said: This issue has three aspects: First: that he returns in repentance and regret, then he is not punished by consensus. Second: that he returns without repentance and persists in what he did, then he is punished by consensus. Third: that his return is not known for any reason, then it is subject to the mentioned difference. (2) His statement 'he is disgraced and not punished': its apparent meaning is that tashhir is not ta'zir, when in fact it is a type of ta'zir. Indeed, Shuraih used to disgrace and not punish corporally; he would send him to his market if he was a market person, or to his people if he was not a market person at their gathering, and say: 'We found him a false witness, so beware of him and warn the people.' This is agreed upon, as in al-Fath quoting al-Mughni. And his statement 'he is not punished' means without beating, because tashhir is ta'zir. In sum, there is agreement on ta'zir, but he sufficed with disgracing his situation in the markets, and that may be more severe than a light beating, and they added beating to that. Hence in al-Minh: Whoever appears to have testified falsely is punished with tashhir. (1) His statement: 'Indeed Shuraih...' is a proof for the Imam's madhhab. If you say: apparently the Imam followed Shuraih, who is a Tabi'i, and the Imam does not accept following a Tabi'i. I say: the origin of the proof is citing the consensus of the Companions, because Shuraih was a judge in the time of the Companions, and such tashhir was not hidden from the Companions, and none of them objected, so it took the place of consensus. Moreover, Shuraih, although a Tabi'i, the Companions allowed him to exercise ijtihad and referred to his statement in debate. So one who is of this status among the leading Tabi'is, his ruling is like the ruling of the Companions. It is even reported that the Imam followed them and counted among them like Masruq, al-Hasan, 'Alqama, and Shuraih, and those of their rank. So in reality, this is following the Companions because they permitted their action and statement, especially Shuraih, as he was a judge during the time of 'Umar and the caliphs after him, so his action was famous among them. How could it not be when it was in their presence? So following him is necessarily following them. (2) His statement 'He sends him...' said in al-Hidayah: The explanation of tashhir is transmitted from Shuraih: he would send him to his market if he was a market person, and to his people if he was not a market person after 'Asr.
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling for someone who confesses to having given false testimony. The matn states that such a person is to be publicly disgraced (yushahhar) but not physically beaten (lam yu'azzar). The commentary explains that this disgrace is a form of ta'zir (discretionary punishment) and is implemented by the judge by announcing the person's offense in public places. The text distinguishes between different scenarios: if the confessor repents sincerely, no punishment is given; if he persists, punishment is applied; if his state is unknown, there is disagreement. The evidence for this ruling is the practice of Shuraih, a famous judge from the time of the Companions, who used to disgrace false witnesses without beating. The commentator argues that this practice amounts to an implicit consensus (ijma) of the Companions because they did not object to it. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that tashhir alone is sufficient, though some later scholars added beating. The commentary also addresses the objection that following a Tabi'i (like Shuraih) is not permissible in the Hanafi school, explaining that in this case it is effectively following the Companions who approved his practice.

Key Terms
شهادة الزور (shahada al-zur): The act of testifying falsely in court, i.e., perjury.
تشهير (tashhir): Public disgrace or humiliation, specifically announcing the person's offense in public places.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the punishment for someone who confesses to having given false testimony deliberately?
A) He is only beaten (ta'zir bi al-darb).
B) He is publicly disgraced (tashhir) but not beaten.
C) He is imprisoned for a fixed term.
D) He is exiled from his town.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes public disgrace (tashhir) as the punishment for a deliberate confessor of perjury, based on the practice of Shuraih and implicit consensus, and this constitutes a valid form of ta'zir without beating.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Ta'zir of False Witnesses: Tashhir vs. Beatings and Imprisonment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on punishment for false witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on ta'zir for false witnesses (tashhir only vs. beating and imprisonment) and evaluate the evidence from Shuraih and Umar.

Core Idea
For a false witness, Imam Abu Hanifa prescribes tashhir alone; the Sahibayn add beating and imprisonment.

This passage explores an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the appropriate ta'zir for a false witness. The core question: is public disgrace (tashhir) sufficient, or must it be accompanied by corporal punishment and imprisonment? The issue pits the practice of the Tabi'i judge Shuraih (endorsed by Imam Abu Hanifa) against the practice of Caliph Umar (cited by the Sahibayn and Shafi'i). Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the boundaries of judicial discretion and the role of siyasah in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
What is the offense? False witness (shahid zur). What is the required punishment? Ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The dispute is over the specific form of ta'zir.
2
State the Imam's Position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that tashhir (public disgrace) alone suffices; no beating or imprisonment. His evidence is the practice of Shuraih (a Tabi'i judge) who would publicly shame the false witness without beating.
Shuraih's practice was tacitly approved by the Companions, forming a kind of consensus.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the false witness should be given a painful beating and imprisoned. They also accept tashhir as part of ta'zir (per Sarakhsi). Their evidence is the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who flogged a false witness forty lashes, blackened his face, shaved his head, and imprisoned him.
Shafi'i agrees with the Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the Response to Umar's Evidence
The Imam's followers argue that Umar's action was siyasah (state policy) for the public interest, not a prescribed ta'zir. They point out that the forty lashes would reach the hadd of qadhf (slander), which is impermissible for ta'zir, and the blackening of the face is a form of muthlah (disfigurement), which is prohibited.
Some later scholars restricted muthlah to limb mutilation, leaving blackening as permissible siyasah.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The commentary favors Imam Abu Hanifa's view, noting that tashhir may be more severe than a hidden beating and avoids the issues with Umar's action. The relied-upon position is tashhir only.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

فإن شريحاً كان يُشَهرُ ولا يعزّر ، فيبعثُهُ إلى سوقه إن كان سوقياً، وإلى قومه إن كان غير سوقي عند اجتماعهم، فيقول : إنا أخذناه شاهد زور فاحذروه، وحذروه النَّاسِ اتفاقاً ، كما في «الفتح» (۱) معزياً إلى «المغني». وإنّما قوله : لا يعزر بلا ضرب ؛ لأنَّ التشهير تعزير، والحاصل الاتفاق على تعزير غير أنه اكتفى بتشهير حاله في الأسواق ، وقد يكون ذلك أشدُّ من ضربة خفية، وهما أضافا إلى ذلك الضرب. انتهى. ومن ثم قال في «المنح (۲) : من ظهر أنه شهد بزور عزّر بالتشهير. انتهى. كقوله لم : يعزر ، إما بمعنى لم يضرب، أو بتقدير لم يعزّر بالضرب. [1] قوله : وقالا : يوجعه ضرباً ويحبسه ؛ وذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي له إنه يشهر عندهما أيضاً، والتعزير والحبس على قدر ما يراه القاضي عندهما ، كذا في «الهداية» (۲)، وذكروا أن أكثر التعزير تسعة وثلاثون، وأقله ثلاث جلدات. وقال أبو يوسف : يبلغ التعزير خمساً وسبعين سوطاً، وإن رأى الإمام أن يضم إلى الضرب في التعزير الحبس فعل. [٢] قوله : فإن عمر الخ؛ روى ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه» في «الحدود»: عن الوليد بن أبي ملك : «إنَّ عمر الله كتب إلى عماله بالشام في شاهد الزور يضربُ أربعين سوطاً ويُسَخَّمُ وَجهُه ، ويحلق رأسه ، ويطال حبسه» (۳). والجواب من جانب الإمام عن هذا الاستدلال ؛ لأنَّ حديث عمر ه محمول على السياسة، بدلالته التبليغ إلى الأربعين، فإنّه لو كان على سبيل التعزير لم يبلغ الأربعين ؛ لبلوغه حداً في غيره، وبدلالة التسخيم، فإنّه مُثْلَة، وقد ورد النهي عنها. وقد أجاب ابن الهمام عن كونِهِ مُثْلَة، إنَّ المُثْلَةَ ليست إلا في الأعضاء، ومن المشايخ من أجاب عن فعل عمر له بأنه كان سياسة ، فإذا رآه الحاكم ذلك كان له أن يفعله، وقد استفيد منه أنَّ السياسةَ ما يفعله الحاكم لمصلحة العامة من غير ورودِ الشرع. هذا محصل ما في بعض رسائل صاحب «البحر». [٣] قوله : وسَخَّمَ وجهه ؛ - بالخاء المعجمة - ، كما في أكثر النسخ ، مـن السُّخام على وزن الغُراب، بمعنى سوادِ ،القدر، يقال: سَخَّمَ الرجلُ وجهه : سوده بالسُّخام. كذا في «المصباح»(4).
For Shuraih used to publicly disgrace [the false witness] and not ta'zir [by beating]. He would send him to his market if he was a market-person, and to his people if he was not a market-person at their gathering, and say: 'We have found him to be a false witness, so beware of him and warn the people.' It is agreed upon, as in al-Fath quoting from al-Mughni. His statement 'he does not ta'zir' means no beating, because tashhir (public disgrace) IS a ta'zir. The summary is agreement on ta'zir, but he sufficed with tashhir of his state in the markets, and that may be more severe than a hidden beating. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) added beating to that. End. And from that he said in al-Minh: 'Whoever is proven to have given false testimony, he is ta'zired by tashhir.' End. Like his statement: 'he did not ta'zir' either meaning he did not beat, or with the nuance: he did not ta'zir by beating. [1] His statement: 'Indeed Shuraih...' etc.; this is evidence for the Imam's madhhab. If you say: Apparently the Imam followed Shuraih, and he is a Tabi'i, and the Imam does not see following a Tabi'i. I say: The basis of the evidence is by arguing with the consensus of the Companions, because Shuraih was a judge during the time of the Companions, and such tashhir would not be hidden from the Companions, and none of them objected to him, so it takes the place of consensus. Moreover, Shuraih, though a Tabi'i, the Companions permitted him to exercise ijtihad and referred to his statements in debate. Whoever is of this status among the leading Tabi'in, his ruling is like the ruling of the Companions. It is even narrated that the Imam used to follow them and counted among them: Masruq, al-Hasan, Alqamah, Shuraih, and those of their rank. So in reality this is following the Companions, because they allowed his action and statement, especially Shuraih, who was a judge during the time of Umar and the caliphs after him, so his action was well-known among them. How could it not be, as it was done in their presence? So following him is necessarily following them. [2] His statement: 'He would send him...' etc.; Al-Hidayah says: The interpretation of tashhir is transmitted from Shuraih, that he would send him to his market if he was a market-person, and to his people if he was not a market-person after Asr. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He should be given painful beating and imprisoned. And this is the view of al-Shafi'i. Because Umar flogged a false witness forty lashes, blackened his face, and so on. They say: Shuraih sends you greetings and says: We have found this one a false witness, so beware of him and warn people against him. End. As reported by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan in Kitab al-Athar. [1] His statement: 'And the two said: He should be given painful beating and imprisoned.' Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned that according to them he is also publicly disgraced, and ta'zir and imprisonment are according to what the judge sees, as in al-Hidayah. They mentioned that the maximum ta'zir is thirty-nine [lashes] and the minimum is three lashes. Abu Yusuf said: Ta'zir can reach seventy-five lashes, and if the Imam sees to combine beating and imprisonment in ta'zir, he may do so. [2] His statement: 'Indeed Umar...'; Ibn Abi Shayba narrated in his Musannaf in the book of Hudud from al-Walid ibn Abi Muttalib: 'Umar wrote to his governors in Syria concerning the false witness: He is to be flogged forty lashes, his face blackened, his head shaved, and his imprisonment prolonged.' (3) The response from the side of the Imam to this evidence is that the hadith of Umar is interpreted as siyasah (state policy), indicated by the number forty, because if it were by way of ta'zir it would not reach forty, as it would reach the hadd of slander (qadhf) in other cases, and indicated by the blackening of the face, which is muthlah (disfigurement), and there is a prohibition against it. Ibn al-Humam answered the issue of muthlah by saying that muthlah is only on limbs (cutting). Some mashayikh answered that Umar's action was siyasah, so if the ruler sees fit to do it, he may. It is derived from this that siyasah is what the ruler does for the public interest without a specific textual ruling. This is the gist from some treatises of the author of al-Bahr. [3] His statement: 'Sakhkham wajhahu' – with a khā' mu'jamah (pointed khā'), as in most copies, from sukhām (soot) meaning blackness of the pot. It is said: sahhama the man his face: he blackened it with soot. As in al-Misbah.
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ta'zir (discretionary punishment) for a false witness (shahid zur). The lesson begins by presenting Imam Abu Hanifa's position, which relies on the practice of Shuraih (a reputable Tabi'i judge). The Imam's view is that the false witness should be subjected to tashhir (public disgrace) without beating: he is paraded in his market or among his people, and people are warned about him. The commentator explains that this is still considered a ta'zir because tashhir itself is a form of ta'zir. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the false witness should be given a painful beating and imprisoned. They cite the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who flogged a false witness forty lashes, blackened his face, shaved his head, and imprisoned him for a long time. The Imam's response to this evidence is that Umar's action was not a prescribed ta'zir but rather siyasah (state policy) for the public interest. The number forty would reach the hadd of qadhf (slander), which indicates it is not ta'zir, and the blackening of the face involves muthlah (disfigurement), which is prohibited. However, some later scholars note that muthlah only applies to limbs, and blackening the face may be permitted as siyasah. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the text is the Imam's view, as tashhir alone is sufficient and often more deterrent. The passage also discusses details of the Sahibayn's position: maximum ta'zir (39 lashes, though Abu Yusuf allows up to 75), minimum (3 lashes), and the judge's discretion. Overall, the text presents the Imam's evidence from Shuraih's practice (supported by tacit consensus of the Companions) and answers the opposing evidence from Umar's practice.

Key Terms
تشهير (tashhir): Publicizing the crime of a false witness by parading him in his market or among his people and warning others about him.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd or that fall short of hadd requirements.
مثلة (muthlah): Disfigurement of the body, especially by cutting or maiming limbs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this passage, what is the proper ta'zir for a false witness?
A) Flogging forty lashes and blackening the face
B) Public disgrace (tashhir) without beating
C) Beatings and imprisonment only
D) Exile and confiscation of property

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi for false witnesses is tashhir (public disgrace) based on Shuraih's practice, although the Sahibayn and Shafi'i allow beating and imprisonment as siyasah.
